So I took the thirty pieces of silver and threw them into the house of the LORD, to the potter" (11:7-13).

The thirty pieces of silver. Fulfilled when Judas betrays Jesus for thirty pieces of silver (Matthew 26:15; 27:3-10). God decreed the exact price of betrayal 500 years before it happened.

"Awake, O sword, against my shepherd, against the man who stands next to me, declares the LORD of hosts. Strike the shepherd, and the sheep will be scattered; I will turn my hand against the little ones" (13:7).

Jesus quotes this the night of His arrest: "You will all fall away because of me this night. For it is written, 'I will strike the shepherd, and the sheep of the flock will be scattered'" (Matthew 26:31).

"I will strike the shepherd"—God decrees the striking of His own shepherd (Jesus). The crucifixion is God's action, not just human evil. The disciples' scattering is predicted. All decreed and fulfilled exactly.

**Spirit of Grace Poured Out (Zechariah 12:10):** "And I will pour out on the house of David and the inhabitants of Jerusalem a spirit of grace and pleas for mercy, so that, when they look on me, on him whom they have pierced, they shall mourn for him." Repentance is the result of God's poured-out Spirit. God pours; they respond. The mourning follows the pouring—it doesn't precede it.

---

### Malachi: Jacob Loved, Esau Hated

**Election Before Action (Malachi 1:2-3):** "I have loved Jacob but Esau I have hated." Paul quotes this in Romans 9:13 immediately after stating that election was "before they had been born or had done anything either good or bad" (Rom 9:11). Election is unconditional, based on God's sovereign choice, not foreseen action.

**God Does Not Change (Malachi 3:6):** "For I the LORD do not change; therefore you, O children of Jacob, are not consumed." God's immutability is the basis for Israel's preservation. They deserve consumption (judgment), but they are "not consumed" because "I the LORD do not change." God's character, purposes, and covenant promises are unchanging. If God changed, His covenant could fail. But He doesn't change, so His elect are preserved. This connects to James 1:17: "Every good gift and every perfect gift is from above, coming down from the Father of lights, with whom there is no variation or shadow due to change."

**God's Treasured Possession (Malachi 3:16-17):** "Then those who feared the LORD spoke with one another. The LORD paid attention and heard them, and a book of remembrance was written before him of those who feared the LORD and esteemed his name. 'They shall be mine, says the LORD of hosts, in the day when I make up my treasured possession, and I will spare them as a man spares his son who serves him.'" "They shall be mine"—definite possession. "In the day when I make up my treasured possession"—God is gathering His elect, His special possession (cf. Titus 2:14; 1 Peter 2:9). "I will spare them"—guaranteed preservation based on their status as God's treasured possession, not their merit. A "book of remembrance" is written—parallel to the Lamb's book of life (Revelation 13:8; 20:12, 15; 21:27). Those whose names are written are spared. Election, writing, preservation—all God's sovereign work.

---

### Summary of Attacks on Israel

**Egyptian Bondage Predicted and Executed (Genesis 15:13-16):** Already added in Patch 1, but emphasize: 400 years of bondage predicted before Isaac is born. God decrees Israel's suffering and deliverance centuries in advance.

**Wilderness Wandering Decreed (Numbers 14:28-35):** "Say to them, 'As I live, declares the LORD, what you have said in my hearing I will do to you: your dead bodies shall fall in this wilderness, and of all your number, listed in the census from twenty years old and upward, who have grumbled against me, not one shall come into the land where I swore that I would make you dwell, except Caleb the son of Jephunneh and Joshua the son of Nun... According to the number of the days in which you spied out the land, forty days, a year for each day, you shall bear your iniquity forty years, and you shall know my displeasure'" (14:28-29, 34).

God decrees that the entire generation will die in the wilderness over 40 years. The decree is specific (all over 20 except Caleb and Joshua) and certain. God's judgment is executed exactly as spoken.

**Midianite Oppression (Judges 6:1-2, 6):** "The people of Israel did what was evil in the sight of the LORD, and the LORD gave them into the hand of Midian seven years. And the hand of Midian overpowered Israel" (6:1-2). "And Israel was brought very low because of Midian. And the people of Israel cried out for help to the LORD" (6:6).

"The LORD gave them into the hand of Midian"—God's active judgment. Israel's cry prompts God's deliverance through Gideon (covered in Patch 23).

**Philistine Oppression (Judges 13:1):** "And the people of Israel again did what was evil in the sight of the LORD, so the LORD gave them into the hand of the Philistines for forty years."

Forty years under Philistine dominance. God gives them over. Deliverance begins with Samson (13:5).

**Assyrian Invasion and Exile of Northern Kingdom (2 Kings 17:6-23; 18:9-12):** "In the ninth year of Hoshea, the king of Assyria captured Samaria, and he carried the Israelites away to Assyria... And this occurred because the people of Israel had sinned against the LORD their God, who had brought them up out of the land of Egypt... Therefore the LORD was very angry with Israel and removed them out of his sight. None was left but the tribe of Judah only... The LORD rejected all the descendants of Israel and afflicted them and gave them into the hand of plunderers, until he had cast them out of his sight" (17:6, 7, 18, 20).

"The LORD was very angry... removed them... rejected... afflicted them... gave them into the hand... cast them out of his sight." Six divine actions. The exile is God's decreed judgment, not historical accident. Assyria is God's instrument (Isaiah 10:5-6).

**Sennacherib's Siege of Jerusalem Decreed and Ended (2 Kings 18-19; Isaiah 36-37):** Sennacherib besieges Jerusalem. Hezekiah prays. God responds through Isaiah: "Have you not heard that I determined it long ago? I planned from days of old what now I bring to pass, that you should turn fortified cities into heaps of ruins... I know your sitting down and your going out and coming in, and your raging against me. Because you have raged against me and your complacency has come to my ears, I will put my hook in your nose and my bit in your mouth, and I will turn you back on the way by which you came" (19:25, 27-28).

Already covered in Patch 7, but emphasize: God decreed Assyria's conquests "long ago," and now decrees Jerusalem's deliverance. That night: "And that night the angel of the LORD went out and struck down 185,000 in the camp of the Assyrians" (19:35). One angel, one night, 185,000 dead. God's power is absolute.

**Babylonian Siege and Exile Predicted and Executed (2 Kings 20:16-18; 24:1-4; 25:1-21):** Isaiah prophesies to Hezekiah: "Behold, the days are coming, when all that is in your house, and that which your fathers have stored up till this day, shall be carried to Babylon. Nothing shall be left, says the LORD. And some of your own sons, who will come from you, whom you will father, shall be taken away, and they shall be eunuchs in the palace of the king of Babylon" (20:17-18).

Decreed 100+ years before it happens. The exile is certain.

When it comes: "In his days, Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon came up, and Jehoiakim became his servant for three years. Then he turned and rebelled against him. And the LORD sent against him bands of the Chaldeans and bands of the Syrians and bands of the Moabites and bands of the Ammonites, and sent them against Judah to destroy it, according to the word of the LORD that he spoke by his servants the prophets. Surely this came upon Judah at the command of the LORD, to remove them out of his sight, for the sins of Manasseh, according to all that he had done" (24:1-3).

"The LORD sent... at the command of the LORD... to remove them." God's decreed judgment executed through Babylon.

The final siege (25:1-21): Jerusalem falls, temple destroyed, people exiled—exactly as prophesied for 100+ years through multiple prophets (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Ezekiel). God's word is certain; His decrees are executed.

**70 Years of Exile Decreed (Jeremiah 25:11-12; 29:10):** "This whole land shall become a ruin and a waste, and these nations shall serve the king of Babylon seventy years. Then after seventy years are completed, I will punish the king of Babylon and that nation, the land of the Chaldeans, for their iniquity, declares the LORD" (25:11-12).

Specific duration: 70 years. Not approximate—exact. God decrees the length of exile and the timing of return. Fulfilled precisely (Ezra 1:1; Daniel 9:2).

---

## VI. The Gospels: Sovereignty Incarnate

### Matthew: The King's Sovereign Authority

**Definite Atonement (Matthew 1:21)**: "She will bear a son, and you shall call his name Jesus, for he will save his people from their sins." Not "he will try to save" or "make salvation possible for"—"he WILL save." Guaranteed accomplishment, not potential possibility. And not potentially everyone, but "HIS people"—a definite group whom He will definitely save. The angel doesn't say "all people" or "whoever believes"—the scope is defined: His people.

**Sovereign Calling (Matthew 4:18-22; 9:9)**: "While walking by the Sea of Galilee, he saw two brothers, Simon (who is called Peter) and Andrew his brother, casting a net into the sea, for they were fishermen. And he said to them, 'Follow me, and I will make you fishers of men.' Immediately they left their nets and followed him... As Jesus passed on from there, he saw a man called Matthew sitting at the tax booth, and he said to him, 'Follow me.' And he rose and followed him."

Jesus initiates. He sees, He calls, they follow. No negotiation, no human initiative. "Follow me"—command, not invitation. "Immediately they left"—the call produces the response. Later Jesus says: "You did not choose me, but I chose you" (John 15:16). The calling effectually produces obedience.

**Sovereign Providence Over Sparrows (Matthew 10:29-31)**: "Are not two sparrows sold for a penny? And not one of them will fall to the ground apart from your Father. But even the hairs of your head are all numbered. Fear not, therefore; you are of more value than many sparrows."

Not one sparrow falls "apart from your Father"—nothing happens outside God's sovereign decree, not even the death of insignificant birds. Not "God permits sparrows to fall" but "not one will fall apart from your Father"—active sovereignty over every event. "The hairs of your head are all numbered"—exhaustive knowledge implies exhaustive control. If God sovereignly ordains every sparrow's fall and numbers every hair, how much more does He ordain the salvation of His elect?

**Revelation by Divine Choice (Matthew 11:25-27)**: "At that time Jesus declared, 'I thank you, Father, Lord of heaven and earth, that you have hidden these things from the wise and understanding and revealed them to little children; yes, Father, for such was your gracious will. All things have been handed over to me by my Father, and no one knows the Father except the Son and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him.'"

God actively hides truth from some ("you have hidden these things from the wise") and reveals to others ("revealed them to little children"). Not "the wise rejected what was offered equally" but "you have hidden"—active concealment. The criterion is not human wisdom or seeking—it is God's "gracious will" (eudokia—good pleasure, sovereign purpose).

"No one knows the Father except the Son and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him"—revelation is selective, not universal. Jesus "chooses to whom he will reveal"—not based on who seeks, but based on His sovereign choice. This is sovereign election in revelation: God determines who receives spiritual understanding.

**Parables Hide and Reveal (Matthew 13:10-17)**: "Then the disciples came and said to him, 'Why do you speak to them in parables?' And he answered them, 'To you it has been given to know the secrets of the kingdom of heaven, but to them it has not been given. For to the one who has, more will be given, and he will have an abundance, but from the one who has not, even what he has will be taken away. This is why I speak to them in parables, because seeing they do not see, and hearing they do not hear, nor do they understand. Indeed, in their case the prophecy of Isaiah is fulfilled that says: "You will indeed hear but never understand, and you will indeed see but never perceive. For this people's heart has grown dull, and with their ears they can barely hear, and their eyes they have closed, lest they should see with their eyes and hear with their ears and understand with their heart and turn, and I would heal them." But blessed are your eyes, for they see, and your ears, for they hear.'"

"To you it has been given to know the secrets of the kingdom of heaven, but to them it has not been given"—passive voice, divine action. Understanding is given by God, not achieved by human effort. "To them it has not been given"—God withholds understanding from some.

"This is why I speak to them in parables"—purpose clause. Jesus uses parables not to clarify but to conceal. Parables reveal truth to those with eyes to see (the elect) and hide truth from those without (the reprobate). This is judicial hardening—judgment for prior unbelief and for God's sovereign purposes.

Isaiah's prophecy: "hearing they do not hear"—they have ears but cannot understand. This is the same judicial hardening as Romans 9-11, John 12:39-40, and Acts 28:25-27. God hardens some through the very preaching of the Word.

**Revelation Given by the Father (Matthew 16:17)**: "And Jesus answered him, 'Blessed are you, Simon Bar-Jonah! For flesh and blood has not revealed this to you, but my Father who is in heaven.'"

Peter's confession ("You are the Christ, the Son of the living God," 16:16) didn't originate from human insight ("flesh and blood") but from divine revelation ("my Father... revealed"). Spiritual understanding is God's gift, not human discovery. No human reasoning or investigation produces saving faith—only divine revelation.

**Unless the Father Builds (Matthew 18:19-20)**: While not explicitly about salvation, Jesus' teaching on corporate prayer demonstrates God's sovereign involvement: "Again I say to you, if two of you agree on earth about anything they ask, it will be done for them by my Father in heaven. For where two or three are gathered in my name, there am I among them." The Father grants requests—prayer succeeds because God acts, not because human agreement compels Him.

**Seats Prepared by the Father (Matthew 20:23)**: "He said to them, 'You will drink my cup, but to sit at my right hand and at my left is not mine to grant, but it is for those for whom it has been prepared by my Father.'"

Positions in the kingdom are "prepared by my Father"—predetermined, assigned by God's sovereign will before creation. Not earned, not chosen by humans, but prepared by the Father for those He has chosen. Even Jesus (in His human nature) doesn't unilaterally grant positions—the Father has predetermined who receives what.

**Many Called, Few Chosen (Matthew 22:14)**: "For many are called, but few are chosen." Clear distinction between the general call (external gospel proclamation to many) and effectual election (God's choosing of few). Not everyone who hears the gospel is chosen; election is particular, selective, sovereign. The "many" hear; the "few" are effectually chosen and saved.

**The Great Judgment (Matthew 25:31-46)**: "When the Son of Man comes in his glory, and all the angels with him, then he will sit on his glorious throne. Before him will be gathered all the nations, and he will separate people one from another as a shepherd separates the sheep from the goats. And he will place the sheep on his right, but the goats on the left. Then the King will say to those on his right, 'Come, you who are blessed by my Father, inherit the kingdom prepared for you from the foundation of the world'... Then he will say to those on his left, 'Depart from me, you cursed, into the eternal fire prepared for the devil and his angels.'"

Two groups: sheep (elect) and goats (reprobate). Jesus does the separating—human choice doesn't determine the category. "Come, you who are blessed by my Father"—blessing comes from the Father, not human merit. "Inherit the kingdom prepared for you from the foundation of the world"—the kingdom was prepared for specific people before creation. Not "the kingdom was prepared and whoever chooses can inherit"—it was prepared FOR THEM specifically, before they existed.

The good works (feeding hungry, clothing naked, etc.) don't earn salvation—they prove it. The sheep didn't know they were serving Christ (25:37-39), yet they did it. Why? Because God worked in them to do His will (Philippians 2:13). The works are fruit, not root.

**Decree and Woe (Matthew 26:24)**: "The Son of Man goes as it is written of him, but woe to that man by whom the Son of Man is betrayed! It would have been better for that man if he had not been born."

"As it is written"—the crucifixion is decreed, written in Scripture in advance (Psalm 41:9; Isaiah 53; Zechariah 11:12-13). Yet "woe to that man"—Judas is held responsible. Divine decree and human culpability are both affirmed without explanation or contradiction. The decree doesn't remove guilt; it accomplishes God's purpose through human sinful action. God ordains the end (Christ's death) and the means (Judas' betrayal), yet Judas is guilty.

"It would have been better for that man if he had not been born"—Judas' damnation is so severe that non-existence would be preferable. This refutes any suggestion that all are ultimately saved or that hell is temporary.

**All Authority Given (Matthew 28:18-20)**: "And Jesus came and said to them, 'All authority in heaven and on earth has been given to me. Go therefore and make disciples of all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father and of the Son and of the Holy Spirit, teaching them to observe all that I have commanded you. And behold, I am with you always, to the end of the age.'"

"All authority in heaven and on earth has been given to me"—absolute sovereignty. Jesus possesses all authority over all creation—nothing falls outside His control. The Great Commission rests on Christ's authority. "Make disciples"—command given, but who responds? Those appointed to eternal life (Acts 13:48), those whose hearts the Lord opens (Acts 16:14), those granted to come to Christ (John 6:65).

"I am with you always, to the end of the age"—Christ's presence guarantees perseverance. He doesn't abandon His people; He preserves them to the end by His presence and power.

---

### Mark: The Suffering Servant's Sovereign Power

**Jesus Appoints the Twelve (Mark 3:13-15)**: "And he went up on the mountain and called to him those whom he desired, and they came to him. And he appointed twelve (whom he also named apostles) so that they might be with him and he might send them out to preach and have authority to cast out demons."

"He called to him those **whom he desired**"—Jesus chooses according to His will, not their merit or request. "And they came to him"—His call is effectual. Those He calls, come. This is sovereign election to apostleship.

**The Secret Given to Some (Mark 4:11-12)**: "To you has been given the secret of the kingdom of God, but for those outside everything is in parables, so that 'they may indeed see but not perceive, and may indeed hear but not understand, lest they should turn and be forgiven.'"

"Has been given"—passive voice, God gives. "For those outside"—some are inside, some outside by divine determination. The parables conceal truth from those outside "lest they should turn and be forgiven"—judicial hardening with purpose clause. God prevents conversion for those not chosen. This parallels Matthew 13:10-17 and fulfills Isaiah's prophecy of hardening.

**Authority Over Creation (Mark 4:35-41; 6:45-52)**: Jesus commands the storm: "Peace! Be still!" and "the wind ceased, and there was a great calm." He walks on water, defying natural law. The disciples ask: "Who then is this, that even the wind and the sea obey him?" Nature obeys its Creator. If Christ sovereignly controls wind, waves, and all creation, how much more does He control salvation?

**Authority Over Demons and Death (Mark 5:1-20; 5:35-42)**: Legion cannot act without Christ's permission—"So he gave them permission." Demons operate only within God's sovereign decree. Jesus raises Jairus's daughter by command: "Talitha cumi... I say to you, arise." Death obeys. He has sovereign power over spiritual forces and physical death.

**Help My Unbelief (Mark 9:23-24)**: When the father of the demon-possessed boy says "If you can do anything, have compassion on us and help us," Jesus replies: "If you can! All things are possible for one who believes." The father cries: "I believe; help my unbelief!"

The father acknowledges his faith is weak and needs divine help. Even faith itself requires God's help—"help my unbelief!" We cannot generate sufficient faith on our own; God must grant it.

**Who Can Be Saved? (Mark 10:23-27)**: After the rich young ruler leaves, Jesus says: "How difficult it will be for those who have wealth to enter the kingdom of God!... It is easier for a camel to go through the eye of a needle than for a rich person to enter the kingdom of God."

The disciples ask: "Then who can be saved?" Jesus' answer: "With man it is impossible, but not with God. For all things are possible with God."

Salvation is **impossible with man**—total inability explicitly stated. Salvation is **possible with God**—not merely enabled by God, but accomplished by God. If salvation depended on human cooperation, it would still be "with man" and therefore impossible. But it's "with God" alone—monergistic. God's sovereign power saves those man cannot save.

**Ransom for Many (Mark 10:45)**: "For even the Son of Man came not to be served but to serve, and to give his life as a ransom for many."

"A ransom for many"—not "for all," but "for many." Definite atonement. Christ's death ransoms (purchases, redeems) a specific group—the elect, "the many." His death actually accomplishes redemption for those for whom He died; it doesn't merely make salvation possible for everyone.

**The Stone the Builders Rejected (Mark 12:10-11)**: "Have you not read this Scripture: 'The stone that the builders rejected has become the cornerstone; this was the Lord's doing, and it is marvelous in our eyes'?"

Jesus quotes Psalm 118:22-23. The rejection of the Messiah and His exaltation are both "the Lord's doing"—God's sovereign plan. Human rejection of Christ becomes the means of salvation—the rejected stone becomes the cornerstone.

**Decree and Responsibility (Mark 14:21)**: "For the Son of Man goes as it is written of him, but woe to that man by whom the Son of Man is betrayed! It would have been better for that man if he had not been born."

"As it is written"—the crucifixion is decreed, scripted in Scripture before it happened. Yet "woe to that man"—Judas is held responsible. Divine decree and human culpability both affirmed without explanation. The decree doesn't remove guilt; it accomplishes God's purpose through human sinful action.

**Not My Will, But Yours (Mark 14:36)**: "And he said, 'Abba, Father, all things are possible for you. Remove this cup from me. Yet not what I will, but what you will.'"

"All things are possible for you"—God's omnipotence. "Not what I will, but what you will"—submission to God's decreed plan. Even Christ's human will submits to the Father's sovereign decree. The cross was God's will, decreed before the foundation of the world (Acts 2:23; 4:27-28; Revelation 13:8).

---

### Luke: Hidden and Revealed by Divine Will

**Born King of the Jews (Luke 1:31-33)**: "And behold, you will conceive in your womb and bear a son, and you shall call his name Jesus. He will be great and will be called the Son of the Most High. And the Lord God will give to him the throne of his father David, and he will reign over the house of Jacob forever, and of his kingdom there will be no end."

Not "he might reign if people accept him," but "he will reign"—guaranteed. "Of his kingdom there will be no end"—sovereign, eternal reign decreed before birth.

**Nothing Impossible With God (Luke 1:37)**: "For nothing will be impossible with God." God's omnipotence—no limitation on His power. If God can bring about a virgin birth, He can certainly accomplish salvation monergistically.

**God Has Visited and Redeemed (Luke 1:68-79)**: Zechariah's prophecy: "Blessed be the Lord God of Israel, for he has visited and redeemed his people and has raised up a horn of salvation for us in the house of his servant David, as he spoke by the mouth of his holy prophets from of old, that we should be saved from our enemies and from the hand of all who hate us; to show the mercy promised to our fathers and to remember his holy covenant, the oath that he swore to our father Abraham, to grant us that we, being delivered from the hand of our enemies, might serve him without fear, in holiness and righteousness before him all our days."

"He has visited and redeemed"—past tense, accomplished decree. "As he spoke by the mouth of his holy prophets from of old"—predetermined salvation, prophesied in advance. "To remember his holy covenant, the oath that he swore"—covenant salvation based on God's oath, not human cooperation. God swears to accomplish it; He will keep His oath.

**God Moves Caesar's Decree (Luke 2:1-2)**: "In those days a decree went out from Caesar Augustus that all the world should be registered. This was the first registration when Quirinius was governor of Syria."

Caesar thinks he's ordering a census for taxation. God is moving him to fulfill Micah 5:2—the Messiah must be born in Bethlehem. God sovereignly orchestrates pagan rulers to accomplish His purposes. Caesar's autonomous decree serves God's predetermined plan.

**Prophets Sent to Specific People (Luke 4:25-27)**: "But in truth, I tell you, there were many widows in Israel in the days of Elijah, when the heavens were shut up three years and six months, and a great famine came over all the land, and Elijah was sent to none of them but only to Zarephath, in the land of Sidon, to a woman who was a widow. And there were many lepers in Israel in the time of the prophet Elisha, and none of them was cleansed, but only Naaman the Syrian."

God's selective mercy. "Many widows in Israel"—Elijah sent to none of them, but to one Gentile widow. "Many lepers in Israel"—Elisha cleansed none of them, but one Gentile leper. Why? God's sovereign choice. He shows mercy to whom He wills (Romans 9:15). The Jews listening to this were so enraged they tried to throw Jesus off a cliff (Luke 4:28-29)—because sovereign election offends human pride.

**Secrets Given, Secrets Hidden (Luke 8:10)**: "He said, 'To you it has been given to know the secrets of the kingdom of God, but for others they are in parables, so that "seeing they may not see, and hearing they may not understand."'"

Parallel to Matthew 13:11-17 and Mark 4:11-12. "To you it has been given"—passive, divine action. Understanding is granted to some, withheld from others. "For others they are in parables"—purpose: conceal truth from the non-elect. "So that seeing they may not see"—judicial hardening. God uses parables to hide truth from those He has not chosen.

**Father's Gracious Will (Luke 10:21-22)**: "In that same hour he rejoiced in the Holy Spirit and said, 'I thank you, Father, Lord of heaven and earth, that you have hidden these things from the wise and understanding and revealed them to little children; yes, Father, for such was your gracious will. All things have been handed over to me by my Father, and no one knows who the Son is except the Father, or who the Father is except the Son and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him.'"

Same as Matthew 11:25-27. God actively hides truth from some ("you have hidden") and reveals to others ("revealed them to little children"). The criterion is not human wisdom, effort, or seeking—it is "your gracious will" (eudokia—sovereign good pleasure). 

"No one knows who the Father is except the Son and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him"—revelation is selective. Jesus chooses to whom He reveals the Father. Not everyone who hears has the Father revealed to them—only those Jesus sovereignly chooses.

**Sparrows Not Forgotten (Luke 12:6-7)**: "Are not five sparrows sold for two pennies? And not one of them is forgotten before God. Why, even the hairs of your head are all numbered. Fear not; you are of more value than many sparrows."

Parallel to Matthew 10:29-31 but with emphasis: "not one of them is forgotten before God." God's comprehensive knowledge and care extend to every sparrow. If God numbers every hair and remembers every sparrow, He sovereignly ordains everything. Nothing falls outside His decree.

**God's Sovereignty in Apparent Randomness (Luke 13:1-5)**: "There were some present at that very time who told him about the Galileans whose blood Pilate had mingled with their sacrifices. And he answered them, 'Do you think that these Galileans were worse sinners than all the other Galileans, because they suffered in this way? No, I tell you; but unless you repent, you will all likewise perish. Or those eighteen on whom the tower in Siloam fell and killed them: do you think that they were worse offenders than all the others who lived in Jerusalem? No, I tell you; but unless you repent, you will all likewise perish.'"

When people die in what seems like random tragedy (Pilate's massacre, tower collapse), the question is: were they worse sinners? Jesus' answer: No, but all deserve judgment. Implication: these deaths were not random accidents outside God's control, but within His providence. God sovereignly determines who dies and when, even in what appears to be accident or evil human action. The point: repent, because death can come at God's appointed time without warning.

**Narrow Door, Many Seek But Cannot (Luke 13:23-24)**: "And someone said to him, 'Lord, will those who are saved be few?' And he said to them, 'Strive to enter through the narrow door. For many, I tell you, will seek to enter and will not be able.'"

"Many... will seek to enter and will not be able"—seeking is not sufficient. Many will try to enter the kingdom and fail. Why? Because entrance requires God's sovereign grant, not human effort. Human seeking without divine election doesn't save.

**God Humbles and Exalts (Luke 14:11; 18:14)**: "For everyone who exalts himself will be humbled, and he who humbles himself will be exalted" (14:11). "For everyone who exalts himself will be humbled, but the one who humbles himself will be exalted" (18:14, after the Pharisee and tax collector parable).

God does the humbling and exalting—passive voice. God opposes the proud and gives grace to the humble (James 4:6; 1 Peter 5:5). But who humbles himself? Those whom God grants a humble heart (the tax collector's repentance is God-given).

**Impossible With Man, Possible With God (Luke 18:24-27)**: "Jesus, seeing that he had become sad, said, 'How difficult it is for those who have wealth to enter the kingdom of God! For it is easier for a camel to go through the eye of a needle than for a rich person to enter the kingdom of God.' Those who heard it said, 'Then who can be saved?' But he said, 'What is impossible with man is possible with God.'"

Context: salvation. "What is impossible with man"—total inability explicitly stated. Self-salvation is impossible. "Is possible with God"—God can do what man cannot. Salvation is not man cooperating with God's enablement; it's God accomplishing what man cannot accomplish. Monergistic.

**Satan Demands, Jesus Prays, Faith Doesn't Fail (Luke 22:31-32)**: "Simon, Simon, behold, Satan demanded to have you, that he might sift you like wheat, but I have prayed for you that your faith may not fail. And when you have turned again, strengthen your brothers."

Satan wants to destroy Peter's faith. Jesus prays that Peter's "faith may not fail"—and it doesn't. Not "I prayed that you would maintain your faith" (synergistic), but "I prayed that your faith may not fail" (monergistic). Christ's intercession guarantees Peter's perseverance. "When you have turned again"—not "if," but "when." Peter's restoration is certain because of Christ's effective intercession.

This is the doctrine of perseverance: Christ prays for His elect (John 17:9—"I am praying for them. I am not praying for the world but for those whom you have given me"), and His prayers are always answered (John 11:42). Therefore, the elect will persevere to the end.

**Decree and Responsibility (Luke 22:22)**: "For the Son of Man goes as it has been determined, but woe to that man by whom he is betrayed!"

Jesus's betrayal was decreed ("as it has been determined"—perfect passive participle, formally decided). Yet Judas is held responsible ("woe to that man"). Divine decree and human culpability coexist without contradiction—this is the consistent biblical pattern throughout Scripture.

**Christ Had to Suffer (Luke 24:25-27, 44-47)**: "And he said to them, 'O foolish ones, and slow of heart to believe all that the prophets have spoken! Was it not necessary that the Christ should suffer these things and enter into his glory?' And beginning with Moses and all the Prophets, he interpreted to them in all the Scriptures the things concerning himself... Then he said to them, 'These are my words that I spoke to you while I was still with you, that everything written about me in the Law of Moses and the Prophets and the Psalms must be fulfilled.' Then he opened their minds to understand the Scriptures, and said to them, 'Thus it is written, that the Christ should suffer and on the third day rise from the dead, and that repentance for the forgiveness of sins should be proclaimed in his name to all nations, beginning from Jerusalem.'"

"Was it not necessary that the Christ should suffer"—divine necessity, decreed plan. "Everything written about me... must be fulfilled"—all of Scripture (Law, Prophets, Psalms—the entire Old Testament) points to Christ and His necessary suffering and glory. "Must be fulfilled"—divine decree written in advance, certain to come to pass.

"Then he opened their minds to understand the Scriptures"—even understanding Scripture requires divine action. The disciples couldn't understand until Christ sovereignly "opened their minds." Spiritual comprehension is God's gift, not human achievement. This is the same principle as "no one knows the Father except the Son and anyone to whom the Son chooses to reveal him" (10:22).

---

### John: Born Not of Human Will, But of God

John's Gospel contains the most explicit statements of sovereign, monergistic grace in all four Gospels. Every major discourse returns to the same themes: spiritual life comes from above, human will is enslaved until freed by God, and those given to Christ will infallibly come to Him.

**Birth Not of Human Will (John 1:12-13)**: "But to all who did receive him, who believed in his name, he gave the right to become children of God, who were born, not of blood nor of the will of the flesh nor of the will of man, but of God."

Three negatives, one positive. Birth as God's child is NOT of:
1. Blood (natural descent)
2. The will of the flesh (human nature)
3. The will of man (human choice)

But OF GOD. Regeneration is monergistic—God's will alone, not man's. If birth as God's child depended on human will, this verse would be false.

**You Must Be Born Again (John 3:3, 5-8)**: "Jesus answered him, 'Truly, truly, I say to you, unless one is born again he cannot see the kingdom of God'... 'Truly, truly, I say to you, unless one is born of water and the Spirit, he cannot enter the kingdom of God. That which is born of the flesh is flesh, and that which is born of the Spirit is spirit. Do not marvel that I said to you, "You must be born again." The wind blows where it wishes, and you hear its sound, but you do not know where it comes from or where it goes. So it is with everyone who is born of the Spirit.'"

Birth precedes sight and entrance. You must be born to see—the order matters. The new birth is compared to wind: sovereign, beyond human control. "The wind blows where IT wishes"—not where we direct it. So is everyone born of the Spirit—the Spirit sovereignly regenerates whom He wills.

**Nothing Unless Given From Heaven (John 3:27)**: "John answered, 'A person cannot receive even one thing unless it is given him from heaven.'"

If a person cannot receive even ONE thing unless given from heaven, then faith itself must be given. This applies universally—all reception depends on heavenly giving.

**Jesus Gives Life to Whom He Wills (John 5:21, 25-29)**: "For as the Father raises the dead and gives them life, so also the Son gives life to whom he will... Truly, truly, I say to you, an hour is coming, and is now here, when the dead will hear the voice of the Son of God, and those who hear will live. For as the Father has life in himself, so he has granted the Son also to have life in himself... Do not marvel at this, for an hour is coming when all who are in the tombs will hear his voice and come out, those who have done good to the resurrection of life, and those who have done evil to the resurrection of judgment."

"The Son gives life to whom he will"—not to everyone equally, but "to whom he will"—sovereign choice. "The dead will hear the voice of the Son of God, and those who hear will live"—spiritual resurrection. The dead cannot hear until Christ makes them hear. Then they live. Monergistic regeneration.

**All Given Will Come (John 6:37)**: "All that the Father gives me will come to me, and whoever comes to me I will never cast out."

The giving precedes and ensures the coming. "ALL that the Father gives... WILL come." Not "might come" or "are enabled to come"—WILL come. This is effectual calling. The Father's giving guarantees the result. And those who come are never cast out—perseverance is certain.

**Jesus Loses None (John 6:39)**: "And this is the will of him who sent me, that I should lose nothing of all that he has given me, but raise it up on the last day."

Success is guaranteed. Jesus will lose NOTHING—not "I hope not to lose any" but "I should lose nothing." Particular, effectual atonement with guaranteed preservation.

**No One Can Come Unless Drawn (John 6:44)**: "No one can come to me unless the Father who sent me draws him. And I will raise him up on the last day."

"No one CAN"—universal inability. Coming to Christ requires the Father's drawing. And notice: everyone the Father draws, Jesus raises up. Drawing is effectual, not merely possible. If drawing only made salvation possible but didn't guarantee it, Jesus couldn't promise to "raise him up"—the "him" is the one drawn.

**No One Can Come Unless Granted (John 6:65)**: "And he said, 'This is why I told you that no one can come to me unless it is granted him by the Father.'"

Coming must be granted. It is not a natural human ability—it is a divine gift. The context (6:60-66) shows many disciples turning back because this teaching is hard. They stumble over the doctrine of sovereign grace.

**Words Are Spirit and Life (John 6:63)**: "It is the Spirit who gives life; the flesh is no help at all. The words that I have spoken to you are spirit and life."

"The flesh is no help at all"—total inability. Human nature contributes zero to salvation. "The Spirit gives life"—monergistic regeneration. Only the Spirit can make alive; the flesh cannot assist.

**Jesus Knows Who Will Believe (John 6:64)**: "But there are some of you who do not believe.' (For Jesus knew from the beginning who those were who did not believe, and who it was who would betray him.)"

Jesus knew "from the beginning" who would believe and who wouldn't. This is foreknowledge (divine omniscience), but in context it's causative—Jesus knows because He's enacting the Father's purpose (6:37-44).

**Slaves to Sin, Freed by the Son (John 8:31-36)**: "So Jesus said to the Jews who had believed him, 'If you abide in my word, you are truly my disciples, and you will know the truth, and the truth will set you free.' They answered him, 'We are offspring of Abraham and have never been enslaved to anyone. How is it that you say, "You will become free"?' Jesus answered them, 'Truly, truly, I say to you, everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin. The slave does not remain in the house forever; the son remains forever. So if the Son sets you free, you will be free indeed.'"

"Everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin"—slavery, not freedom. The unregenerate are enslaved, unable to free themselves. "If the Son sets you free, you will be free indeed"—Christ must do the freeing. Not human cooperation, but divine liberation.

**Being "Of God" Precedes Hearing (John 8:43-47)**: "Why do you not understand what I say? It is because you cannot bear to hear my word. You are of your father the devil, and your will is to do your father's desires... Whoever is of God hears the words of God. The reason why you do not hear them is that you are not of God."

Being "of God" is the cause; hearing is the effect. Not "you're not of God because you don't hear"—"you don't hear BECAUSE you are not of God." Spiritual receptivity depends on prior divine action (regeneration).

**You Don't Believe Because You're Not My Sheep (John 10:24-30)**: "So the Jews gathered around him and said to him, 'How long will you keep us in suspense? If you are the Christ, tell us plainly.' Jesus answered them, 'I told you, and you do not believe. The works that I do in my Father's name bear witness about me, but you do not believe because you are not among my sheep. My sheep hear my voice, and I know them, and they follow me. I give them eternal life, and they will never perish, and no one will snatch them out of my hand. My Father, who has given them to me, is greater than all, and no one is able to snatch them out of the Father's hand. I and the Father are one.'"

The order is critical. Jesus does NOT say: "You're not my sheep because you don't believe." He says: "You don't believe BECAUSE you are not among my sheep."

Sheep-status precedes believing. Being "of the sheep" is the cause; believing is the effect. And the sheep are given by the Father (10:29), hear Christ's voice (10:27), are known by Him (10:27), follow Him (10:27), receive eternal life (10:28), and will never perish (10:28). Every element is certain—because it all flows from the Father's sovereign giving.

**Lazarus Raised: Life-Giving Command (John 11:1-44)**: When Lazarus dies, Jesus declares: "I am the resurrection and the life. Whoever believes in me, though he die, yet shall he live, and everyone who lives and believes in me shall never die" (11:25-26).

At the tomb, Jesus prays publicly (11:41-42), then commands: "Lazarus, come out" (11:43). "The man who had died came out, his hands and feet bound with linen strips, and his face wrapped with a cloth. Jesus said to them, 'Unbind him, and let him go'" (11:44).

Lazarus was dead—totally unable to respond. Jesus spoke; Lazarus lived and came out. This is a picture of monergistic regeneration: the spiritually dead cannot respond until Christ speaks life into them. The dead don't cooperate in resurrection; they're raised by sovereign power.

**You Did Not Choose Me (John 15:16)**: "You did not choose me, but I chose you and appointed you that you should go and bear fruit and that your fruit should abide, so that whatever you ask the Father in my name, he may give it to you."

The priority is explicit: "You did NOT choose me, but I chose you." Christ's choice precedes and produces the disciples' following. Election is sovereign, not responsive.

**Jesus Prays for Those Given to Him (John 17:2, 6, 9, 20, 24)**: Jesus's high priestly prayer is for a particular group:
- 17:2: "Since you have given him authority over all flesh, to give eternal life to all whom you have given him."
- 17:6: "I have manifested your name to the people whom you gave me out of the world. Yours they were, and you gave them to me."
- 17:9: "I am praying for them. I am not praying for the world but for those whom you have given me, for they are yours."
- 17:20: "I do not ask for these only, but also for those who will believe in me through their word."
- 17:24: "Father, I desire that they also, whom you have given me, may be with me where I am."

Five times Jesus refers to "those whom you have given me." This is particular atonement and intercession—not for the world generally, but for the elect specifically. The prayer's confidence (17:24: "I desire") flows from the certainty that the Father always hears Him (11:42).

**Judicial Hardening (John 12:37-40)**: "Though he had done so many signs before them, they still did not believe in him, so that the word spoken by the prophet Isaiah might be fulfilled: 'Lord, who has believed what he heard from us, and to whom has the arm of the Lord been revealed?' Therefore they could not believe. For again Isaiah said, 'He has blinded their eyes and hardened their heart, lest they see with their eyes, and understand with their heart, and turn, and I would heal them.'"

After witnessing many signs, they "could not believe." Why? Because God "blinded their eyes and hardened their heart." The purpose clause ("lest they... turn and I would heal them") shows God preventing conversion. This is judicial hardening to fulfill Isaiah 6:9-10.

**Judas' Betrayal Foreknown (John 13:18-19, 21-30)**: "I am not speaking of all of you; I know whom I have chosen. But the Scripture will be fulfilled, 'He who ate my bread has lifted his heel against me.' I am telling you this now, before it takes place, that when it does take place you may believe that I am he... After saying these things, Jesus was troubled in his spirit, and testified, 'Truly, truly, I say to you, one of you will betray me.'"

"I know whom I have chosen"—Jesus chose the Twelve, including Judas (for a different purpose). Jesus predicts the betrayal before it happens so they will believe. Judas' betrayal is within God's decree (Acts 2:23; 4:27-28).

**I Am the Way (John 14:6)**: "Jesus said to him, 'I am the way, and the truth, and the life. No one comes to the Father except through me.'"

Exclusive claim: "No one comes to the Father except through me." Christ is the only way—no other path to God exists.

**Greater Works Because I Go to the Father (John 14:12-14)**: "Truly, truly, I say to you, whoever believes in me will also do the works that I do; and greater works than these will he do, because I am going to the Father. Whatever you ask in my name, this I will do, that the Father may be glorified in the Son."

Christ's departure enables greater works through the Spirit. Prayer in Jesus' name is powerful because Christ accomplishes it ("this I will do").

**The Spirit Sent by the Father (John 14:16-17, 26)**: "And I will ask the Father, and he will give you another Helper, to be with you forever, even the Spirit of truth, whom the world cannot receive, because it neither sees him nor knows him. You know him, for he dwells with you and will be in you... But the Helper, the Holy Spirit, whom the Father will send in my name, he will teach you all things and bring to your remembrance all that I have said to you."

The Father sends the Spirit at Christ's request. "The world cannot receive" Him—total inability of the unregenerate to receive the Spirit. The Spirit teaches and reminds—sovereign work producing understanding.

**Vine and Branches: Total Dependence (John 15:1-11)**: "I am the true vine, and my Father is the vinedresser. Every branch in me that does not bear fruit he takes away, and every branch that does bear fruit he prunes, that it may bear more fruit. Already you are clean because of the word that I have spoken to you. Abide in me, and I in you. As the branch cannot bear fruit by itself, unless it abides in the vine, neither can you, unless you abide in me. I am the vine; you are the branches. Whoever abides in me and I in him, he it is that bears much fruit, for apart from me you can do nothing."

"Apart from me you can do nothing"—absolute dependence. The branch has no life, no fruit, no ability apart from the vine. This is total dependence on Christ for spiritual life and fruitfulness. "You can do **nothing**"—zero autonomous spiritual productivity.

**You Did Not Choose Me (John 15:16, 19)**: "You did not choose me, but I chose you and appointed you that you should go and bear fruit and that your fruit should abide, so that whatever you ask the Father in my name, he may give it to you... If you were of the world, the world would love you as its own; but because you are not of the world, but I chose you out of the world, therefore the world hates you."

Twice: "I chose you." The priority is explicit—Christ's choice precedes and produces the disciples' following. "I chose you out of the world"—sovereign election separates believers from the world.

**The Spirit Convicts the World (John 16:7-11)**: "Nevertheless, I tell you the truth: it is to your advantage that I go away, for if I do not go away, the Helper will not come to you. But if I go, I will send him to you. And when he comes, he will convict the world concerning sin and righteousness and judgment: concerning sin, because they do not believe in me; concerning righteousness, because I go to the Father, and you will see me no longer; concerning judgment, because the ruler of this world is judged."

The Spirit convicts—God's active work exposing sin, revealing righteousness, warning of judgment. Conviction is the Spirit's sovereign work, not human self-discovery.

**The Spirit Guides Into All Truth (John 16:13-15)**: "When the Spirit of truth comes, he will guide you into all the truth, for he will not speak on his own authority, but whatever he hears he will speak, and he will declare to you the things that are to come. He will glorify me, for he will take what is mine and declare it to you. All that the Father has is mine; therefore I said that he will take what is mine and declare it to you."

The Spirit guides believers into truth—active divine leading, not autonomous human discovery. The Spirit glorifies Christ by revealing Him. Understanding is the Spirit's gift.

**Jesus' High Priestly Prayer (John 17:1-26)**: The most comprehensive prayer for particular election in Scripture.

**Authority Over All Flesh to Give Eternal Life (17:1-3)**: "Father, the hour has come; glorify your Son that the Son may glorify you, since you have given him authority over all flesh, to give eternal life to all whom you have given him. And this is eternal life, that they know you, the only true God, and Jesus Christ whom you have sent."

"You have given him authority over all flesh, to give eternal life to all whom you have given him"—Christ has universal authority, but gives eternal life to a particular group: "all whom you have given him." Definite atonement explicitly stated.

**Manifested Your Name to Those You Gave Me (17:6-10)**: "I have manifested your name to the people whom you gave me out of the world. Yours they were, and you gave them to me, and they have kept your word. Now they know that everything that you have given me is from you. For I have given them the words that you gave me, and they have received them and have come to know in truth that I came from you; and they have believed that you sent me. I am praying for them. I am not praying for the world but for those whom you have given me, for they are yours."

"The people whom you gave me out of the world"—particular group, given by the Father. "Yours they were, and you gave them to me"—they belonged to the Father, He gave them to Christ. "I am not praying for the world but for those whom you have given me"—Christ's intercession is for the elect specifically, not humanity generally.

**Keep Them in Your Name (17:11-12)**: "And I am no longer in the world, but they are in the world, and I am coming to you. Holy Father, keep them in your name, which you have given me, that they may be one, even as we are one. While I was with them, I kept them in your name, which you have given me. I have guarded them, and not one of them has been lost except the son of destruction, that the Scripture might be fulfilled."

Christ kept the disciples; now He prays the Father will keep them. "Not one of them has been lost except the son of destruction"—Judas' loss fulfills Scripture, doesn't contradict Christ's power to preserve. The elect are kept; Judas was never elect (13:18: "I know whom I have chosen").

**Sanctify Them in the Truth (17:17-19)**: "Sanctify them in the truth; your word is truth. As you sent me into the world, so I have sent them into the world. And for their sake I consecrate myself, that they also may be sanctified in truth."

The Father sanctifies through the Word. Christ consecrates Himself (sets Himself apart for sacrifice) so they may be sanctified. Sanctification is God's work, not self-improvement.

**Those Who Will Believe Through Their Word (17:20-23)**: "I do not ask for these only, but also for those who will believe in me through their word, that they may all be one, just as you, Father, are in me, and I in you, that they also may be in us, so that the world may believe that you have sent me."

Christ prays for future believers—"those who will believe." Future tense certainty: they **will** believe. The elect's coming to faith is certain because Christ prays for them and the Father always hears Him (11:42).

**Father, I Desire That They Be With Me (17:24-26)**: "Father, I desire that they also, whom you have given me, may be with me where I am, to see my glory that you have given me because you loved me before the foundation of the world... I made known to them your name, and I will continue to make it known, that the love with which you have loved me may be in them, and I in them."

"Whom you have given me"—fifth time in this chapter referencing the Father's giving. "I desire that they... may be with me"—Christ's will aligned with Father's decree. The elect will be glorified because Christ desires it and the Father gave them. Perseverance and glorification are certain.

**No Authority Except From Above (John 19:10-11)**: "Pilate said to him, 'You will not speak to me? Do you not know that I have authority to release you and authority to crucify you?' Jesus answered him, 'You would have no authority over me at all unless it had been given you from above. Therefore he who delivered me over to you has the greater sin.'"

Pilate's authority is derivative—"given from above." Even the crucifixion occurs under God's sovereign decree (Acts 2:23; 4:27-28). Human agents are responsible ("he who delivered me... has the greater sin"), but God's decree encompasses their actions.

**It Is Finished (John 19:30)**: "When Jesus had received the sour wine, he said, 'It is finished,' and he bowed his head and gave up his spirit."

"It is finished" (Greek: *tetelestai*—paid in full, completed). The atonement is accomplished, not merely made possible. Christ's work saves all for whom He died—the elect given by the Father.

**Thomas Believes (John 20:24-29)**: Thomas doubts the resurrection until Jesus appears to him personally. Jesus says, "Put your finger here, and see my hands; and put out your hand, and place it in my side. Do not disbelieve, but believe" (20:27). Thomas responds: "My Lord and my God!" (20:28).

Jesus creates faith by revealing Himself. Thomas believes because Christ appeared—divine initiative produces response. "Blessed are those who have not seen and yet have believed" (20:29)—but even those who believe without seeing do so because God grants faith.

**Purpose Statement (John 20:30-31)**: "Now Jesus did many other signs in the presence of the disciples, which are not written in this book; but these are written so that you may believe that Jesus is the Christ, the Son of God, and that by believing you may have life in his name."

John's Gospel is written to produce faith. But the instrument (written Word) is effective only when God opens hearts to receive it (Acts 16:14). The Word is the means; God's power is the cause.

**Feed My Sheep (John 21:15-17)**: Three times Jesus asks Peter, "Do you love me?" Three times Peter affirms love. Three times Jesus commands: "Feed my lambs... Tend my sheep... Feed my sheep."

Christ's sheep need feeding—they're dependent on shepherding, teaching, care. Believers depend on Christ's provision through under-shepherds. Total dependence from regeneration through glorification.  

---

## VII. Acts: Sovereignty in Mission

### Crucifixion by Definite Plan

**Acts 2:23**: "This Jesus, delivered up according to the definite plan and foreknowledge of God, you crucified and killed by the hands of lawless men."

Human action ("you crucified") and divine decree ("according to the definite plan") both affirmed. The crucifixion wasn't Plan B after human rebellion—it was Plan A from eternity.

**Acts 4:27-28**: "For truly in this city there were gathered together against your holy servant Jesus, whom you anointed, both Herod and Pontius Pilate, along with the Gentiles and the peoples of Israel, to do whatever your hand and your plan had predestined to take place."

Everything the conspirators did against Jesus, they did to fulfill what God's "hand and plan had predestined." Even the greatest evil in history (deicide) was within God's sovereign decree. Yet all parties are held responsible (2:23: "you crucified").

### Appointed to Eternal Life Believed

**Acts 13:48**: "And when the Gentiles heard this, they began rejoicing and glorifying the word of the Lord, and as many as were appointed to eternal life believed."

The appointment precedes and causes belief. Not "as many as believed were appointed"—"as many as were appointed... believed." Appointment to eternal life is the cause; believing is the effect.

### The Lord Opened Her Heart

**Acts 16:14**: "One who heard us was a woman named Lydia, from the city of Thyatira, a seller of purple goods, who was a worshiper of God. The Lord opened her heart to pay attention to what was said by Paul."

The order: The Lord opened her heart, THEN she paid attention. Heart-opening produces attention and faith, not vice versa. This is monergistic conversion—God acts first; response follows.

### Already His People

**Acts 18:10**: "For I am with you, and no one will attack you to harm you, for I have many in this city who are my people."

Jesus tells Paul that He has "many in this city" who are His people—before they've been evangelized, before they've believed. They are already His in the decree; evangelism gathers them in time.

**The Promise Is for Those God Calls (Acts 2:39):** "For the promise is for you and for your children and for all who are far off, everyone whom the Lord our God calls to himself."

"Everyone whom the Lord our God calls to himself"—the promise extends as far as God's effectual call. The scope is "everyone" God calls, but it's limited to those He calls. Universal language with particular application—all whom God calls will receive the promise.

**God Gives Repentance (Acts 5:31; 11:18):** "God exalted him at his right hand as Leader and Savior, to give repentance to Israel and forgiveness of sins" (5:31). "When they heard these things they fell silent. And they glorified God, saying, 'Then to the Gentiles also God has granted repentance that leads to life'" (11:18).

Repentance is given and granted by God, not self-generated by human will. If repentance must be given, it cannot be produced autonomously. This is monergistic grace—God gives both repentance and faith (Philippians 1:29).

**God Allowed and Commands (Acts 14:16; 17:30):** "In past generations he allowed all the nations to walk in their own ways" (14:16). "The times of ignorance God overlooked, but now he commands all people everywhere to repent" (17:30).

God "allowed" the nations to walk in their own ways—but this allowance was itself God's sovereign administration of history. And now He "commands all people everywhere to repent"—the universal command establishes responsibility and reveals duty, while God's granting repentance (5:31; 11:18) accomplishes the result in the elect.

**God Determines Times and Boundaries (Acts 17:26-27):** "And he made from one man every nation of mankind to live on all the face of the earth, having determined allotted periods and the boundaries of their dwelling place, that they should seek God, and perhaps feel their way toward him and find him. Yet he is actually not far from each one of us."

God "determined allotted periods and the boundaries" of all nations. Times and places for every people group are God's sovereign decree. Purpose: "that they should seek God." Even the seeking is within God's ordained purposes.

**God's Works Known from Eternity (Acts 15:18)**: "Known to God from of old are all his works." (Some translations: "Known to God from eternity are all his works.") God's comprehensive foreknowledge of all His works implies their decreed certainty. If God knows His works from eternity, He predetermined them from eternity.

**Paul's Sovereign Conversion (Acts 9:3-6, 15)**: "Now as he went on his way, he approached Damascus, and suddenly a light from heaven shone around him. And falling to the ground, he heard a voice saying to him, 'Saul, Saul, why are you persecuting me?'... But the Lord said to him, 'Go, for he is a chosen instrument of mine to carry my name before the Gentiles and kings and the children of Israel.'"

Paul wasn't seeking Christ—he was persecuting Him. Christ appeared sovereignly, knocked him down, blinded him, and converted him by irresistible grace. "He is a chosen instrument of mine"—chosen before conversion, chosen for specific purpose. Paul's conversion is the paradigm of monergistic grace: the chief of sinners saved while actively rebelling (1 Timothy 1:13-16).

---

## VIII. Pauline Epistles: Systematic Exposition

### Romans: The Fullest Exposition

Romans is Paul's systematic theology of salvation, demonstrating God's absolute sovereignty from election to glorification, human total inability, and monergistic grace throughout.

**God's Wrath and Judicial Abandonment (Romans 1:18-32)**: "For the wrath of God is revealed from heaven against all ungodliness and unrighteousness of men, who by their unrighteousness suppress the truth." Humans actively suppress truth (1:18), and God responds with threefold judicial abandonment: "God gave them up" (1:24, 26, 28)—active divine judgment, not passive permission. God gives rebels over to their sin as punishment, the same pattern as Pharaoh's hardening.

**Total Depravity (Romans 3:10-20)**: Ten statements of universal corruption: "None is righteous, no, not one; no one understands; no one seeks for God. All have turned aside; together they have become worthless; no one does good, not even one." Explicit: "No one seeks for God"—if no one seeks, then those who come must be drawn by divine initiative (John 6:44). "By works of the law no human being will be justified... through the law comes knowledge of sin"—the law diagnoses but cannot cure.

**Justification by Grace as Gift (Romans 3:21-26)**: "The righteousness of God through faith in Jesus Christ for all who believe... justified by his grace as a gift, through the redemption that is in Christ Jesus, whom God put forward as a propitiation." All divine action—God's righteousness, God's gift, God put forward Christ. Humans receive by faith, but faith itself is God's gift (Ephesians 2:8-9; Philippians 1:29).

**Boasting Excluded (Romans 3:27-28)**: "Then what becomes of our boasting? It is excluded. By what kind of law? By a law of works? No, but by the law of faith. For we hold that one is justified by faith apart from works of the law." Faith excludes all boasting because faith is receiving, not achieving.

**Abraham Justified by Faith, Not Works (Romans 4:1-8)**: "Abraham believed God, and it was counted to him as righteousness" (Genesis 15:6). "Now to the one who works, his wages are not counted as a gift but as his due. And to the one who does not work but believes in him who justifies the ungodly, his faith is counted as righteousness." Critical contrast: works = wages (earned); faith = gift (received). "To the one who does not work but believes"—faith is not a work. "Him who justifies the ungodly"—God justifies the ungodly, not the godly (there are none).

**Promise Rests on Grace (Romans 4:13-17)**: "For the promise to Abraham and his offspring that he would be heir of the world did not come through the law but through the righteousness of faith... That is why it depends on faith, in order that the promise may rest on grace and be guaranteed to all his offspring." Faith is the instrument ensuring the promise rests on grace alone. "God... gives life to the dead and calls into existence the things that do not exist"—the same creative power operative in salvation.

**Federal Headship: Adam and Christ (Romans 5:12-21)**: "Therefore, just as sin came into the world through one man, and death through sin, and so death spread to all men because all sinned." Adam's sin imputed to all his descendants—we sinned in him as our federal head. Proof: "death reigned from Adam to Moses, even over those whose sinning was not like the transgression of Adam" (5:14)—infants and those without explicit law still died, proving inherited guilt.

"As by the one man's disobedience the many were made sinners, so by the one man's obedience the many will be made righteous" (5:19). Both passive—humanity was constituted sinful by Adam's act; the elect are constituted righteous by Christ's act. Neither is human achievement.

**Dead to Sin, Alive to God (Romans 6:1-14)**: "How can we who died to sin still live in it? Do you not know that all of us who have been baptized into Christ Jesus were baptized into his death?" Union with Christ means death to sin's dominion. "We know that our old self was crucified with him in order that the body of sin might be brought to nothing, so that we would no longer be enslaved to sin." Past tense—accomplished. "For sin will have no dominion over you, since you are not under law but under grace"—promise, not potential.

**Slaves to Righteousness (Romans 6:15-23)**: "You who were once slaves of sin have become obedient from the heart to the standard of teaching to which you were committed, and, having been set free from sin, have become slaves of righteousness." Passive voice—God freed them, God enslaved them to righteousness. "For the wages of sin is death, but the free gift of God is eternal life in Christ Jesus our Lord." Wages vs. gift: if eternal life were earned through cooperation, it would be wages, not gift.

**The Law and Indwelling Sin (Romans 7:7-25)**: The law reveals sin but cannot save. "I am of the flesh, sold under sin... For I do not do what I want, but I do the very thing I hate... For I know that nothing good dwells in me, that is, in my flesh." Even believers struggle with remaining sin—"Wretched man that I am! Who will deliver me from this body of death? Thanks be to God through Jesus Christ our Lord!" Deliverance comes through Christ, not self-effort.

**Life in the Spirit (Romans 8:1-17)**: "There is therefore now no condemnation for those who are in Christ Jesus. For the law of the Spirit of life has set you free in Christ Jesus from the law of sin and death." Final verdict: no condemnation. "God has done what the law, weakened by the flesh, could not do. By sending his own Son... he condemned sin in the flesh."

"For the mind that is set on the flesh is hostile to God, for it does not submit to God's law; indeed, it cannot. Those who are in the flesh cannot please God" (8:7-8). Total inability—the unregenerate cannot submit, cannot please God. Not "will not" only, but "cannot."

"For all who are led by the Spirit of God are sons of God... The Spirit himself bears witness with our spirit that we are children of God, and if children, then heirs" (8:14-17). Being led by the Spirit marks sonship. Sonship guarantees inheritance—no "might be heirs," but "if children, then heirs."

**The Golden Chain (Romans 8:28-30)**: "And we know that for those who love God all things work together for good, for those who are called according to his purpose. For those whom he foreknew he also predestined to be conformed to the image of his Son... And those whom he predestined he also called, and those whom he called he also justified, and those whom he justified he also glorified."

Five unbreakable links: Foreknew → Predestined → Called → Justified → Glorified. Every person foreknown is predestined. Every person predestined is called. Every person called is justified. Every person justified is glorified. No dropouts, no failures. Glorification is past tense though future—so certain Paul writes it as accomplished.

**Nothing Can Separate (Romans 8:31-39)**: "What then shall we say to these things? If God is for us, who can be against us? He who did not spare his own Son but gave him up for us all, how will he not also with him graciously give us all things?" Argument from greater to lesser—if God gave Christ, He'll give everything needed for salvation.

"Who shall bring any charge against God's elect? It is God who justifies. Who is to condemn? Christ Jesus is the one who died—more than that, who was raised—who is at the right hand of God, who indeed is interceding for us." No successful accusation possible—God justifies, Christ intercedes.

"For I am sure that neither death nor life, nor angels nor rulers, nor things present nor things to come, nor powers, nor height nor depth, nor anything else in all creation, will be able to separate us from the love of God in Christ Jesus our Lord." Ten categories covering every possible threat. Future tense—nothing will succeed in separating.

**Unconditional Election: Jacob and Esau (Romans 9:10-13)**: "And not only so, but also when Rebekah had conceived children by one man, our forefather Isaac, though they were not yet born and had done nothing either good or bad—in order that God's purpose of election might continue, not because of works but because of him who calls—she was told, 'The older will serve the younger.' As it is written, 'Jacob I loved, but Esau I hated.'"

Paradigm text for unconditional election: (1) not yet born, (2) had done nothing good or bad, (3) purpose: demonstrate election is God's purpose not human achievement, (4) explicit: "not because of works but because of him who calls."

**It Depends on God (Romans 9:14-16)**: "What shall we say then? Is there injustice on God's part? By no means! For he says to Moses, 'I will have mercy on whom I have mercy, and I will have compassion on whom I have compassion.' So then it depends not on human will or exertion, but on God, who has mercy."

Verse 16 demolishes synergism: "It depends not on human will or exertion, but on God, who has mercy." Not on human decision, choice, desire, effort, work, or running. But on God's sovereign mercy alone.

**Pharaoh Hardened (Romans 9:17-18)**: "For the Scripture says to Pharaoh, 'For this very purpose I have raised you up, that I might show my power in you, and that my name might be proclaimed in all the earth.' So then he has mercy on whomever he wills, and he hardens whomever he wills." God raised up Pharaoh for specific purpose, then hardened him. Both mercy and hardening are sovereign acts.

**The Potter's Right (Romans 9:19-21)**: "You will say to me then, 'Why does he still find fault? For who can resist his will?' But who are you, O man, to answer back to God? Will what is molded say to its molder, 'Why have you made me like this?' Has the potter no right over the clay, to make out of the same lump one vessel for honorable use and another for dishonorable use?"

Paul doesn't explain away divine sovereignty when faced with objection—he asserts Creator rights. From the same lump (fallen humanity), God makes some vessels for honor, some for dishonor.

**Vessels of Wrath and Mercy (Romans 9:22-24)**: "What if God, desiring to show his wrath and to make known his power, has endured with much patience vessels of wrath prepared for destruction, in order to make known the riches of his glory for vessels of mercy, which he has prepared beforehand for glory—even us whom he has called, not from the Jews only but also from the Gentiles?"

Two kinds: vessels of wrath (display His justice) and vessels of mercy which "he has prepared beforehand for glory" (display His mercy). Both serve His purpose to display His glory.

**Remnant Chosen by Grace (Romans 11:1-6)**: "God has not rejected his people whom he foreknew... So too at the present time there is a remnant, chosen by grace. But if it is by grace, it is no longer on the basis of works; otherwise grace would no longer be grace."

Grace and works are mutually exclusive. If salvation were partly grace, partly human cooperation, grace would no longer be grace—it would be wages. No mixture possible.

**The Elect Obtained, Rest Hardened (Romans 11:7-10)**: "What then? Israel failed to obtain what it was seeking. The elect obtained it, but the rest were hardened, as it is written, 'God gave them a spirit of stupor, eyes that would not see and ears that would not hear, down to this very day.'"

Two groups: elect (obtained righteousness) and rest (hardened). "God gave them a spirit of stupor"—active divine judicial hardening.

**God's Irrevocable Calling (Romans 11:25-29)**: "Lest you be wise in your own sight, I do not want you to be unaware of this mystery, brothers: a partial hardening has come upon Israel, until the fullness of the Gentiles has come in. And in this way all Israel will be saved... For the gifts and the calling of God are irrevocable."

God's calling cannot be revoked. Whom He calls, He saves. This applies to Israel corporately and individuals—those God calls will persevere.

**All Consigned to Disobedience for Mercy (Romans 11:32-36)**: "For God has consigned all to disobedience, that he may have mercy on all... For from him and through him and to him are all things. To him be glory forever. Amen."

God imprisoned all in disobedience for His purpose: to show mercy. The doxology: "from him and through him and to him are all things"—if salvation were partly from us, this would be false. All is from, through, and to God alone.

**Transformation by Renewal (Romans 12:1-2)**: "I appeal to you therefore, brothers, by the mercies of God, to present your bodies as a living sacrifice... Do not be conformed to this world, but be transformed by the renewal of your mind." The "therefore" points back to chapters 1-11. Commands rest on indicatives—because God saved us monergistically, we respond by His grace. "Be transformed" is passive—God transforms; we submit. Commands don't prove synergism; they prove God works in believers to produce the obedience He commands (Philippians 2:13).

**Submission to Authorities (Romans 13:1-7)**: "Let every person be subject to the governing authorities. For there is no authority except from God, and those that exist have been instituted by God." God sovereignly establishes all governing authorities—even unbelieving rulers serve His purposes.

**Judgment Seat of Christ (Romans 14:10-12)**: "Why do you pass judgment on your brother? Or you, why do you despise your brother? For we will all stand before the judgment seat of God... So then each of us will give an account of himself to God." All believers will give account to God—but our justification is already settled (8:1, 33-34). This judgment concerns rewards and loss of rewards, not salvation status.

**God of Hope (Romans 15:13)**: "May the God of hope fill you with all joy and peace in believing, so that by the power of the Holy Spirit you may abound in hope." Even joy, peace, and hope are produced by God's power through the Spirit—not self-generated human optimism.

---

### 1 Corinthians: The Message of the Cross

**Folly to Perishing, Power to Called (1 Corinthians 1:18, 24)**: "For the word of the cross is folly to those who are perishing, but to us who are being saved it is the power of God... but to those who are called, both Jews and Greeks, Christ the power of God and the wisdom of God."

Two groups: perishing (to whom the cross is folly) and called (to whom Christ is power and wisdom). The difference is the calling—God's effectual call makes the difference.

**God Chose (1 Corinthians 1:26-31)**: "For consider your calling, brothers: not many of you were wise according to worldly standards, not many were powerful, not many were of noble birth. But God chose what is foolish in the world to shame the wise; God chose what is weak in the world to shame the strong; God chose what is low and despised in the world, even things that are not, to bring to nothing things that are, so that no human being might boast in the presence of God."

Three-fold "God chose." Election is God's sovereign work. The purpose: "so that no human being might boast." If salvation depended on human cooperation, boasting would be possible ("at least I cooperated"). Paul eliminates this: "Let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord" (1:31).

**Natural Person Cannot Accept (1 Corinthians 2:14)**: "The natural person does not accept the things of the Spirit of God, for they are folly to him, and he is not able to understand them because they are spiritually discerned."

"Does not accept... is not able to understand"—total inability. The natural man cannot receive spiritual truth. Something must change the person before they can accept—that something is regeneration by the Spirit.

**God Gives Growth (1 Corinthians 3:6-7)**: "I planted, Apollos watered, but God gave the growth. So neither he who plants nor he who waters is anything, but only God who gives the growth."

Growth (conversion, sanctification) is God's work alone. Paul and Apollos are "nothing"—God alone gives the growth.

**What Do You Have That You Did Not Receive? (1 Corinthians 4:7)**: "For who sees anything different in you? What do you have that you did not receive? If then you received it, why do you boast as if you did not receive it?"

Everything—including faith—is received. If faith distinguishes believer from unbeliever, and faith is received (not self-generated), then God's gift makes the difference, not human will.

**Spirit Apportions as He Wills (1 Corinthians 12:11, 18)**: "All these are empowered by one and the same Spirit, who apportions to each one individually as he wills... But as it is, God arranged the members in the body, each one of them, as he chose."

The Spirit distributes gifts "as he wills"; God arranges "as he chose." Sovereign distribution—not based on human merit or choice.

---

### 2 Corinthians: Sufficiency From God, Treasure in Jars of Clay

2 Corinthians emphasizes human weakness and divine power—the perfect setting for declarations of God's sovereign grace.

**Comforted to Comfort (2 Corinthians 1:3-5):** "Blessed be the God and Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, the Father of mercies and God of all comfort, who comforts us in all our affliction, so that we may be able to comfort those who are in any affliction, with the comfort with which we ourselves are comforted by God.
