For as we share abundantly in Christ's sufferings, so through Christ we share abundantly in comfort too."

"God of all comfort"—all comfort originates with God. "Who comforts us"—God is the active agent. The pattern: God comforts us so that we can comfort others. We are instruments of God's comfort, not independent sources.

**Not Sufficient In Ourselves (2 Corinthians 3:4-6):** "Such is the confidence that we have through Christ toward God. Not that we are sufficient in ourselves to claim anything as coming from us, but our sufficiency is from God, who has made us sufficient to be ministers of a new covenant, not of the letter but of the Spirit. For the letter kills, but the Spirit gives life."

"Not that we are sufficient in ourselves"—explicit denial of autonomous ability. "Our sufficiency is from God"—God is the source. If we can't even claim anything as coming from ourselves, then we certainly can't generate saving faith autonomously.

"Who has made us sufficient"—God makes us sufficient; we don't become sufficient through our own effort. "The Spirit gives life"—life is the Spirit's gift, not human achievement.

**The Lord Is the Spirit (2 Corinthians 3:17-18):** "Now the Lord is the Spirit, and where the Spirit of the Lord is, there is freedom. And we all, with unveiled face, beholding the glory of the Lord, are being transformed into the same image from one glory to another. For this comes from the Lord who is the Spirit."

"Where the Spirit of the Lord is, there is freedom"—freedom is the Spirit's work, not autonomous human will exercising itself. True freedom is freedom FROM sin, not freedom TO sin.

"Are being transformed"—passive voice, ongoing. God transforms us. "From one glory to another"—progressive sanctification. "For this comes from the Lord who is the Spirit"—the transformation's source is explicitly stated: the Lord, the Spirit. Not human effort.

**Blinded Minds (2 Corinthians 4:3-4):** "And even if our gospel is veiled, it is veiled to those who are perishing. In their case the god of this world has blinded the minds of the unbelievers, to keep them from seeing the light of the gospel of the glory of Christ, who is the image of God."

The gospel is veiled to "those who are perishing"—definite group. Satan "has blinded the minds of the unbelievers"—but Satan acts only under God's sovereign permission (Job 1:12; 2:6). The blinding serves God's purposes—judicial hardening through Satan's agency.

"To keep them from seeing"—purpose clause. The blinding prevents seeing. Total inability to perceive spiritual truth without divine intervention.

**God Shines In Hearts (2 Corinthians 4:6):** "For God, who said, 'Let light shine out of darkness,' has shone in our hearts to give the light of the knowledge of the glory of God in the face of Jesus Christ."

The same creative power that spoke light into existence ("Let light shine out of darkness," Genesis 1:3) shines into hearts. This is new creation language—ex nihilo. God creates spiritual life where there was none.

"Has shone in our hearts"—God's action, not ours. "To give the light of the knowledge"—God gives knowledge of Himself. This is sovereign, monergistic regeneration using creation-level power.

**Treasure in Jars of Clay (2 Corinthians 4:7):** "But we have this treasure in jars of clay, to show that the surpassing power belongs to God and not to us."

The treasure (gospel, ministry) is in fragile containers (human ministers). Purpose: "to show that the surpassing power belongs to God and not to us." If salvation depended on human cooperation, power would be divided. But Paul is explicit: the power belongs to God ALONE, not to us at all.

**Earthly Tent, Building From God (2 Corinthians 5:1-5):** "For we know that if the tent that is our earthly home is destroyed, we have a building from God, a house not made with hands, eternal in the heavens... He who has prepared us for this very thing is God, who has given us the Spirit as a guarantee."

"A building from God"—resurrection body is God's gift. "He who has prepared us"—God prepares, we receive. "Who has given us the Spirit as a guarantee"—the Spirit is God's down payment, guaranteeing completed salvation.

**New Creation (2 Corinthians 5:17-21):** "Therefore, if anyone is in Christ, he is a new creation. The old has passed away; behold, the new has come. All this is from God, who through Christ reconciled us to himself and gave us the ministry of reconciliation; that is, in Christ God was reconciling the world to himself, not counting their trespasses against them, and entrusting to us the message of reconciliation. Therefore, we are ambassadors for Christ, God making his appeal through us. We implore you on behalf of Christ, be reconciled to God. For our sake he made him to be sin who knew no sin, so that in him we might become the righteousness of God."

**Packed with monergistic theology:**

1. **New creation:** "He is a new creation"—not reformed, improved, or assisted, but created new. This is God's creative act.

2. **All from God:** "All this is from God"—the entire salvation is God's work, not shared with human cooperation.

3. **God reconciled us:** "Who through Christ reconciled us to himself"—God reconciles, we don't reconcile ourselves. Passive recipients of God's reconciling work.

4. **God was reconciling:** "In Christ God was reconciling the world to himself"—God is the actor throughout.

5. **Not counting trespasses:** "Not counting their trespasses against them"—justification. God doesn't count our sin against us because He counted it against Christ.

6. **He made him to be sin:** "For our sake he made him to be sin who knew no sin"—penal substitution. God made Christ sin (imputed our sin to Christ) so that we might become righteousness (God imputes Christ's righteousness to us).

7. **We become the righteousness of God:** "So that in him we might become the righteousness of God"—not our own righteousness, but God's righteousness given to us. This is forensic justification—legal declaration based on Christ's righteousness credited to our account.

**God Opens Hearts (2 Corinthians 6:11-13; 7:1):** While the text says "our heart is wide open" (6:11), the broader context shows God's work producing response. Paul appeals: "Widen your hearts also" (6:13), but immediately grounds it in God's promises: "Since we have these promises, beloved, let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit, bringing holiness to perfection in the fear of God" (7:1).

The promises produce the obedience. God's Word produces the response it commands.

**Godly Grief Produces Repentance (2 Corinthians 7:9-10):** "As it is, I rejoice, not because you were grieved, but because you were grieved into repenting. For you felt a godly grief, so that you suffered no loss through us. For godly grief produces repentance that leads to salvation without regret, whereas worldly grief produces death."

"Godly grief produces repentance"—repentance is the product of God-given grief. "That leads to salvation"—repentance is the instrument of salvation, but it's produced by "godly grief," which is God's work. God grants repentance (Acts 11:18; 2 Timothy 2:25).

**Generous Giving Produced by God's Grace (2 Corinthians 8:1, 7; 9:8, 10-11, 14-15):** "We want you to know, brothers, about the grace of God that has been given among the churches of Macedonia" (8:1). Generous giving is attributed to "the grace of God"—God's work in them.

"But as you excel in everything—in faith, in speech, in knowledge, in all earnestness, and in our love for you—see that you excel in this act of grace also" (8:7). Even excelling in giving is "this act of grace"—God's grace working in them.

"And God is able to make all grace abound to you, so that having all sufficiency in all things at all times, you may abound in every good work" (9:8). God makes grace abound, God provides sufficiency, God enables good works.

"He who supplies seed to the sower and bread for food will supply and multiply your seed for sowing and increase the harvest of your righteousness. You will be enriched in every way to be generous in every way, which through us will produce thanksgiving to God... Thanks be to God for his inexpressible gift!" (9:10-11, 15).

God supplies, God multiplies, God increases, God enriches—all active divine causation. Generosity is the fruit of God's grace working in believers, not autonomous human decision.

**God's Power Perfected in Weakness (2 Corinthians 12:7-10):** "So to keep me from becoming conceited because of the surpassing greatness of the revelations, a thorn was given me in the flesh, a messenger of Satan to harass me, to keep me from becoming conceited. Three times I pleaded with the Lord about this, that it should leave me. But he said to me, 'My grace is sufficient for you, for my power is made perfect in weakness.' Therefore I will boast all the more gladly of my weaknesses, so that the power of Christ may rest upon me. For the sake of Christ, then, I am content with weaknesses, insults, hardships, persecutions, and calamities. For when I am weak, then I am strong."

**Critical theology:**

1. **A thorn was given:** Passive voice—God gave it. Even "a messenger of Satan" serves God's purposes (like Job 1-2).

2. **Purpose: to keep from conceit:** God uses suffering sovereignly to prevent pride. The thorn serves God's sanctifying purpose.

3. **God's grace is sufficient:** Grace isn't merely helpful or enabling—it's **sufficient**. God's grace is enough; human strength adds nothing.

4. **Power made perfect in weakness:** God's power is most clearly seen when human strength is absent. If success depended on human cooperation, God's power would be obscured.

5. **When I am weak, then I am strong:** Paradox of grace. True strength is God's power working through human weakness, not human power cooperating with divine assistance.

**Examine Yourselves (2 Corinthians 13:5):** "Examine yourselves, to see whether you are in the faith. Test yourselves. Or do you not realize this about yourselves, that Jesus Christ is in you?—unless indeed you fail to meet the test!"

"Jesus Christ is in you"—the test of genuine faith is Christ's indwelling, which is God's work (Colossians 1:27). Examining ourselves doesn't produce faith; it reveals whether God has worked faith in us.

---

### Galatians: Called by Grace, Not Works

**Set Apart Before Birth (Galatians 1:15-16)**: "But when he who had set me apart before I was born, and who had called me by his grace, was pleased to reveal his Son to me, in order that I might preach him among the Gentiles, I did not immediately consult with anyone."

Paul's apostleship came from God's sovereign choice, not human commissioning. "Set me apart before I was born"—predestined before existence. "Called me by his grace"—effectual calling, not human decision. "Was pleased to reveal his Son to me"—God's sovereign pleasure (eudokia), not Paul's seeking. Paul was actively persecuting the church when Christ appeared to him (Acts 9). This is monergistic conversion: God set apart, God called, God revealed.

**Not by Human Commission (Galatians 1:1)**: "Paul, an apostle—not from men nor through man, but through Jesus Christ and God the Father, who raised him from the dead."

Paul's authority comes entirely from God, not human appointment. His calling bypasses all human agency—directly from Christ and the Father.

**Gospel Revealed by Jesus Christ (Galatians 1:11-12)**: "For I would have you know, brothers, that the gospel that was preached by me is not man's gospel. For I did not receive it from any man, nor was I taught it, but I received it through a revelation of Jesus Christ."

The gospel itself came by direct revelation from Christ, not human tradition or teaching. Even the content of the gospel is God's sovereign communication, not human discovery.

**Scripture Foresaw (Galatians 3:8)**: "And the Scripture, foreseeing that God would justify the Gentiles by faith, preached the gospel beforehand to Abraham, saying, 'In you shall all the nations be blessed.'"

"Scripture, foreseeing"—personification indicating that behind Scripture is God who foreknew and predetermined the justification of Gentiles. The gospel to Abraham was God's predetermined plan announced in advance. God justified Gentiles by faith because He decreed it, not because He foresaw they would believe independently.

**Cursed by the Law, Redeemed by Christ (Galatians 3:10-14)**: "For all who rely on works of the law are under a curse; for it is written, 'Cursed be everyone who does not abide by all things written in the Book of the Law, and do them.'... Christ redeemed us from the curse of the law by becoming a curse for us—for it is written, 'Cursed is everyone who is hanged on a tree'—so that in Christ Jesus the blessing of Abraham might come to the Gentiles, so that we might receive the promised Spirit through faith."

The law pronounces a curse on all who fail to keep it perfectly—which is everyone (Romans 3:10-20). "Christ redeemed us"—definite accomplishment, not potential possibility. Christ became the curse "for us"—substitutionary atonement for a specific people. The result is certain: "so that we might receive the promised Spirit through faith." Christ's redemption secures the Spirit and faith for the elect.

**The Promise Depends on Faith, Therefore Grace (Galatians 3:18)**: "For if the inheritance comes by the law, it no longer comes by promise; but God gave it to Abraham by a promise."

Law and promise are opposing principles. "God gave it to Abraham by a promise"—unilateral, unconditional grant. Promises depend on the one promising (God), not on the one receiving (Abraham/us). Therefore salvation rests on God's faithfulness, not human performance.

**The Law Our Guardian Until Christ (Galatians 3:23-26)**: "Now before faith came, we were held captive under the law, imprisoned until the coming faith would be revealed. So then, the law was our guardian until Christ came, in order that we might be justified by faith. But now that faith has come, we are no longer under a guardian, for in Christ Jesus you are all sons of God, through faith."

"Before faith came, we were held captive under the law"—enslaved, imprisoned. The law held us captive; we didn't free ourselves. "Until the coming faith would be revealed"—faith came as a historical reality through Christ, then is applied individually by the Spirit's work. "Now that faith has come"—God brought faith; we receive it. "You are all sons of God, through faith"—but faith itself is God's gift (Ephesians 2:8-9; Philippians 1:29).

**Sent Forth at the Appointed Time (Galatians 4:4-7)**: "But when the fullness of time had come, God sent forth his Son, born of woman, born under the law, to redeem those who were under the law, so that we might receive adoption as sons. And because you are sons, God has sent the Spirit of his Son into our hearts, crying, 'Abba! Father!' So you are no longer a slave, but a son, and if a son, then an heir through God."

"When the fullness of time had come"—God's predetermined timing. God sent His Son at the exact moment decreed from eternity. "To redeem those who were under the law"—definite atonement, specific people redeemed. "So that we might receive adoption as sons"—adoption is the goal, accomplished through Christ's redemption.

"Because you are sons, God has sent the Spirit"—the Spirit is given because they are already sons (legally, in the decree). The Spirit doesn't make them sons; He testifies to their already-accomplished sonship. "If a son, then an heir"—certain inheritance for all sons. No son fails to inherit.

**God Knew You (Galatians 4:9)**: "But now that you have come to know God—or rather to be known by God—how can you turn back again to the weak and worthless elementary principles of the world, whose slaves you want to be once more?"

Paul corrects himself: "you have come to know God—or rather to be known by God." The real issue isn't our knowing God (which could imply human initiative), but God knowing us (His electing, covenant love). Compare Amos 3:2: "You only have I known of all the families of the earth." To be known by God is to be chosen, loved, elected by Him.

**Fruit of the Spirit (Galatians 5:22-23)**: "But the fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, patience, kindness, goodness, faithfulness, gentleness, self-control; against such things there is no law."

The virtues that mark Christian life are "fruit of the Spirit"—produced by the Spirit's work, not autonomous human effort. Even sanctification flows from God's empowerment, not self-generated morality. The Spirit produces the fruit; we bear it.

**God Works in the Elect (Galatians 5:5)**: "For through the Spirit, by faith, we ourselves eagerly wait for the hope of righteousness."

"Through the Spirit, by faith"—both the means (Spirit) and instrument (faith) are God's provision. We wait eagerly, but the waiting itself is empowered by the Spirit through faith He supplies.

**New Creation (Galatians 6:15)**: "For neither circumcision counts for anything, nor uncircumcision, but a new creation."

What matters is "new creation"—God's creative act, not human modification. Just as physical creation was ex nihilo (from nothing by God's word), new creation is monergistic—God creates new; we don't renovate ourselves. "If anyone is in Christ, he is a new creation. The old has passed away; behold, the new has come" (2 Corinthians 5:17). God does the creating; we are the created.

---

### Ephesians: Predestined Before the Foundation

**Chosen Before the Foundation (Ephesians 1:3-14)**: The entire opening doxology is a sustained celebration of sovereign grace with a threefold refrain.

"Blessed be the God and Father of our Lord Jesus Christ, who has blessed us in Christ with every spiritual blessing in the heavenly places, even as he chose us in him **before the foundation of the world**, that we should be holy and blameless before him. In love **he predestined us for adoption** to himself as sons through Jesus Christ, **according to the purpose of his will, to the praise of his glorious grace**, with which he has blessed us in the Beloved... In him we have redemption through his blood, the forgiveness of our trespasses, according to the riches of his grace, which he lavished upon us, in all wisdom and insight **making known to us the mystery of his will, according to his purpose**, which he set forth in Christ as a plan for the fullness of time, to unite all things in him, things in heaven and things on earth. In him we have obtained an inheritance, **having been predestined according to the purpose of him who works all things according to the counsel of his will**, so that we who were the first to hope in Christ might be **to the praise of his glory**. In him you also, when you heard the word of truth, the gospel of your salvation, and believed in him, were sealed with the promised Holy Spirit, who is the guarantee of our inheritance until we acquire possession of it, **to the praise of his glory**."

**"Before the foundation of the world"**—election is pre-creation, pre-temporal, unconditional. Not based on foreseen faith or cooperation.

**"He predestined us for adoption"**—adoption is not offered and accepted; it is predestined and accomplished. We were legally adopted in eternity past; regeneration makes that legal status experiential.

**Threefold refrain: "according to the purpose of his will" (v5, 9, 11)**—election, revelation of God's plan, and inheritance all flow from God's sovereign purpose, not human cooperation or decision.

**Threefold purpose: "to the praise of his glorious grace/glory" (v6, 12, 14)**—the ultimate goal is God's glory, not human choice or dignity. If salvation depended on libertarian free will, the praise would be split between God's provision and man's decision.

**"Him who works ALL things according to the counsel of his will"**—absolute sovereignty over all events. Not "most things" or "spiritual things"—ALL things. Nothing falls outside God's sovereign control.

**"The mystery of his will, according to his purpose"**—God reveals the gospel, but revelation itself is sovereign.

**Dead, Made Alive (Ephesians 2:1-10)**: "And you were dead in the trespasses and sins in which you once walked, following the course of this world, following the prince of the power of the air, the spirit that is now at work in the sons of disobedience—among whom we all once lived in the passions of our flesh, carrying out the desires of the body and the mind, and were by nature children of wrath, like the rest of mankind. But God, being rich in mercy, because of the great love with which he loved us, even when we were dead in our trespasses, made us alive together with Christ—by grace you have been saved—and raised us up with him and seated us with him in the heavenly places in Christ Jesus, so that in the coming ages he might show the immeasurable riches of his grace in kindness toward us in Christ Jesus. For by grace you have been saved through faith. And this is not your own doing; it is the gift of God, not a result of works, so that no one may boast. For we are his workmanship, created in Christ Jesus for good works, which God prepared beforehand, that we should walk in them."

**Dead—not sick, not wounded, DEAD.** Spiritually dead people cannot cooperate in their resurrection. A corpse cannot "choose" to come back to life or "not resist" resurrection.

**"Following the prince of the power of the air"**—the unregenerate are under Satan's dominion, enslaved to sin. This is not neutral ground where libertarian choice operates.

**"By nature children of wrath"**—the problem is nature (ontological state), not just bad choices. Nature must be changed before new choices are possible.

**"But God, being rich in mercy"**—the initiative is God's. No "but man, being free to choose" or "but man, not resisting grace."

**"Even when we were dead in our trespasses, made us alive"**—while dead, not after we showed some sign of life. Regeneration precedes faith.

**"Made us alive together with Christ"**—monergistic regeneration. God does the making alive; we are the objects, not the co-agents.

**"By grace you have been saved through faith. And THIS is not your own doing; it is the gift of God."** The demonstrative "this" (τοῦτο, touto) most naturally refers to the entire salvation package. The grammar is neuter, while "faith" (πίστεως, pisteos) is feminine, but neuter demonstratives commonly refer to concepts/ideas/states, not just matching-gender nouns. "This"—the whole salvation-by-grace-through-faith—is the gift. Faith is the instrumental means, but it is God-given, not self-generated human contribution.

**"Not a result of works, so that no one may boast."** If salvation depended on human cooperation (even non-resistance or "accepting"), boasting would be possible ("I cooperated when my neighbor didn't"). Paul eliminates all boasting—salvation is God's work alone from start to finish.

**"We are his workmanship, created in Christ Jesus for good works, which God prepared beforehand, that we should walk in them."** Even our good works post-conversion are God's sovereign preparation. Salvation is monergistic; sanctification has cooperative elements, but even that cooperation flows from God's prior work.

**Sealed by the Spirit (Ephesians 1:13-14)**: "In him you also, when you heard the word of truth, the gospel of your salvation, and believed in him, were sealed with the promised Holy Spirit, who is the guarantee of our inheritance until we acquire possession of it, to the praise of his glory."

Believers are **sealed** with the Holy Spirit. The seal is God's act, not ours. The Spirit is the **"guarantee" (ἀρραβών, arrabon)—down payment, pledge, first installment** of inheritance. Perseverance is guaranteed—God finishes what He starts. You don't "acquire possession" by maintaining your part; God ensures you acquire it because the seal is His guarantee.

**Strengthened by the Spirit (Ephesians 3:14-21)**: Paul prays "that according to the riches of his glory he may grant you to be strengthened with power through his Spirit in your inner being, so that Christ may dwell in your hearts through faith—that you, being rooted and grounded in love, may have strength to comprehend with all the saints what is the breadth and length and height and depth, and to know the love of Christ that surpasses knowledge, that you may be filled with all the fullness of God."

Paul prays for God to grant strength, not for believers to muster strength. Spiritual comprehension and love are Spirit-wrought. "Now to him who is able to do far more abundantly than all that we ask or think, according to the power at work within us, to him be glory"—God's power at work in us exceeds our asking or thinking. Sanctification is empowered by God's sovereign work.

**God's Gifts to the Church (Ephesians 4:7-11)**: "But grace was given to each one of us according to the measure of Christ's gift... And he gave the apostles, the prophets, the evangelists, the shepherds and teachers, to equip the saints for the work of ministry."

Spiritual gifts are Christ's sovereign distribution. "He gave"—not "we chose our gifts." Ministry effectiveness flows from Christ's sovereign gifting, not human capability or choice.

---

### Philippians: God Begins and Completes

**God Will Complete (Philippians 1:6)**: "And I am sure of this, that he who began a good work in you will bring it to completion at the day of Jesus Christ."

God begins the work; God completes it. Perseverance is certain because God's work cannot fail. Not "might complete if you cooperate"—"WILL bring it to completion."

**Faith Granted (Philippians 1:29)**: "For it has been granted to you that for the sake of Christ you should not only believe in him but also suffer for his sake."

Faith is "granted"—it is a gift, not a human achievement. Believing is something granted to us, just as suffering is.

**God Works Both Willing and Working (Philippians 2:12-13)**: "Therefore, my beloved, as you have always obeyed, so now, not only as in my presence but much more in my absence, work out your own salvation with fear and trembling, for it is God who works in you, both to will and to work for his good pleasure."

Command: "work out your salvation." Basis: "for it is God who works in you." God works "both to will and to work"—He produces both the desire (willing) and the action (working). Human activity is real, but it is the result of God's prior and continuous working.

This resolves the tension between human responsibility and divine sovereignty: we work BECAUSE God works in us. Our working out is the evidence and result of God's working in.

---

### Colossians: Made Alive

**Made Alive While Dead (Colossians 2:13)**: "And you, who were dead in your trespasses and the uncircumcision of your flesh, God made alive together with him, having forgiven us all our trespasses."

Again: dead, then made alive. Regeneration precedes faith. God acts on the dead; life is the result.

**All Things Created Through and For Christ (Colossians 1:16-17):** "For by him all things were created, in heaven and on earth, visible and invisible, whether thrones or dominions or rulers or authorities—all things were created through him and for him. And he is before all things, and in him all things hold together."

Christ created "all things"—including thrones, dominions, rulers, authorities (both earthly and spiritual powers). All things were created "for him"—the ultimate purpose of all creation is Christ's glory. "In him all things hold together"—Christ actively sustains all existence moment by moment. If Christ stopped upholding, everything would cease to exist. This is comprehensive sovereignty—creation, purpose, and sustenance all belong to Christ.

**God's Chosen Ones (Colossians 3:12):** "Put on then, as God's chosen ones, holy and beloved, compassionate hearts, kindness, humility, meekness, and patience."

"God's chosen ones"—election language. Believers are God's chosen people, selected by His sovereign will. The ethical imperatives flow from the identity: because you are chosen, put on these virtues.

---

### 1 & 2 Thessalonians: Chosen and Appointed

**God Chose You (1 Thessalonians 1:4)**: "For we know, brothers loved by God, that he has chosen you."

Election is certain: "he has chosen you." Not "he offers, you choose"—HE chose YOU.

**God Chose You (2 Thessalonians 2:13)**: "But we ought always to give thanks to God for you, brothers beloved by the Lord, because God chose you as the firstfruits to be saved, through sanctification by the Spirit and belief in the truth."

"God chose you... to be saved." Salvation is the result of God's choice. "Through sanctification by the Spirit and belief in the truth"—these are the means, but God's choice is the cause.

**Destined for Salvation (1 Thessalonians 5:9)**: "For God has not destined us for wrath, but to obtain salvation through our Lord Jesus Christ."

Destiny is determined by God's decree, not human choice. We are "destined... to obtain salvation"—the outcome is certain.

**God Sends Delusion (2 Thessalonians 2:11-12)**: "Therefore God sends them a strong delusion, so that they may believe what is false, in order that all may be condemned who did not believe the truth but had pleasure in unrighteousness."

Judicial hardening: God sends delusion to those who reject truth. This is active divine causation in judgment, not mere permission.

**God Guards (2 Thessalonians 3:3)**: "But the Lord is faithful. He will establish you and guard you against the evil one."

God's faithfulness guarantees preservation. He will guard—not "might guard if you cooperate."

---

### 1 Timothy: Guarding the Gospel Through Sovereign Grace

**God Our Savior (1 Timothy 1:1):** "Paul, an apostle of Christ Jesus by command of God our Savior and of Christ Jesus our hope."

"God our Savior"—salvation is God's work. This title appears throughout the Pastorals (1:1; 2:3; 4:10; Titus 1:3; 2:10, 13; 3:4). Salvation belongs to God; He accomplishes it.

**Christ Came to Save Sinners (1 Timothy 1:12-16):** "I thank him who has given me strength, Christ Jesus our Lord, because he judged me faithful, appointing me to his service, though formerly I was a blasphemer, persecutor, and insolent opponent. But I received mercy because I had acted ignorantly in unbelief, and the grace of our Lord overflowed for me with the faith and love that are in Christ Jesus. The saying is trustworthy and deserving of full acceptance, that Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners, of whom I am the foremost. But I received mercy for this reason, that in me, as the foremost, Jesus Christ might display his perfect patience as an example to those who were to believe in him for eternal life."

**Packed with monergism:**

1. **Christ gave strength:** "He has given me strength"—Paul's ministry depends on Christ's empowerment.

2. **Christ judged, Christ appointed:** "He judged me faithful, appointing me to his service"—sovereign appointment, not Paul's application.

3. **I received mercy:** "I received mercy"—passive. God gave mercy; Paul received it. Not earned, achieved, or cooperated with.

4. **Grace overflowed:** "The grace of our Lord overflowed for me"—overwhelming, abundant grace. Not trickle-down enablement but overflowing flood.

5. **Faith and love in Christ Jesus:** "With the faith and love that are in Christ Jesus"—these qualities are **in Christ**, not self-generated. We receive them from union with Christ.

6. **Christ came to save:** "Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners"—not "to make salvation possible" or "to offer salvation"—to **save**. Mission statement: accomplish salvation, not merely enable it.

7. **Christ displayed patience:** "That... Jesus Christ might display his perfect patience"—God's purpose in Paul's conversion was to display Christ's patience. The conversion serves God's glory, not Paul's autonomous choice.

8. **Those who were to believe:** "As an example to those who were to believe"—perfect tense participle, indicating predetermined group. Those decreed to believe will believe, using Paul as example.

**Mediator Between God and Men (1 Timothy 2:5-6):** "For there is one God, and there is one mediator between God and men, the man Christ Jesus, who gave himself as a ransom for all, which is the testimony given at the proper time."

"One mediator"—Christ alone. No synergistic cooperation between God and man produces salvation. Christ is the exclusive mediator.

"Who gave himself as a ransom for all"—this "all" must be understood in context. Does "all" mean every individual without exception, or all types of people without distinction? Context decides. Verse 4 says God "desires all people to be saved and to come to the knowledge of the truth." But if "all" means every individual without exception, and God's desires are always fulfilled (Psalm 115:3; Isaiah 46:10), then universalism follows. Since universalism is false (Matthew 25:46), "all" must mean "all types" (Jew and Gentile, slave and free, male and female—cf. 1 Timothy 2:1-2, which emphasizes praying for all kinds, including kings).

Christ ransomed people from all nations, not every individual. This is definite atonement—He actually saves those He ransomed.

**Saved Through Childbearing? (1 Timothy 2:15):** "Yet she will be saved through childbearing—if they continue in faith and love and holiness, with self-control."

This difficult verse doesn't teach salvation by childbearing. Options: (1) Saved (physically preserved) through the childbearing process, (2) Saved (spiritually) through **the** childbearing (Christ's incarnation—salvation comes through the seed of the woman, Genesis 3:15), (3) Her role in childbearing/family is salvific in the sense of displaying God's created order.

Whatever the precise meaning, it can't contradict the rest of Scripture's clear testimony that salvation is by grace through faith apart from works.

**Mystery of Godliness (1 Timothy 3:16):** "Great indeed, we confess, is the mystery of godliness: He was manifested in the flesh, vindicated by the Spirit, seen by angels, proclaimed among the nations, believed on in the world, taken up in glory."

The gospel is a "mystery"—hidden truth now revealed. Christ's incarnation, vindication, proclamation, belief, and ascension are all part of God's sovereign plan. "Believed on in the world"—belief happens because Christ is proclaimed, and the proclamation is part of God's decreed plan.

**Some Will Depart (1 Timothy 4:1):** "Now the Spirit expressly says that in later times some will depart from the faith by devoting themselves to deceitful spirits and teachings of demons."

"The Spirit expressly says"—God predicts apostasy. "Some will depart"—apostasy is certain for some. These are not elect who lose salvation, but false professors whose departure proves they were never truly saved (1 John 2:19: "They went out from us, but they were not of us").

**God Is Savior of All People (1 Timothy 4:10):** "For to this end we toil and strive, because we have our hope set on the living God, who is the Savior of all people, especially of those who believe."

"Savior of all people, especially of those who believe"—"all people" in a general sense (providential care, common grace), but "especially" believers (saving grace). If "Savior of all" meant He saves every individual, "especially" would be meaningless. The distinction: God provides for all, but saves the elect.

**Laid Hold Of by Christ Jesus (1 Timothy 6:12, 19):** "Fight the good fight of the faith. Take hold of the eternal life to which you were called and about which you made the good confession in the presence of many witnesses... thus storing up treasure for themselves as a good foundation for the future, so that they may take hold of that which is truly life."

"To which you were called"—divine calling precedes and produces response. "Take hold" uses active language, but Paul already said Timothy was "laid hold of" by Christ (Philippians 3:12: "that I may lay hold of that for which Christ Jesus has laid hold of me"). Christ grabs us first; we grab what He gives.

### 2 Timothy: Guarding the Deposit Through God's Power

**Grace Given Before the Ages Began (2 Timothy 1:9-10):** "Who saved us and called us to a holy calling, not because of our works but according to his own purpose and grace, which he gave us in Christ Jesus before the ages began, and which now has been manifested through the appearing of our Savior Christ Jesus, who abolished death and brought life and immortality to light through the gospel."

**This is one of Scripture's clearest statements of unconditional election:**

1. **Who saved us:** Past tense—salvation is accomplished, not potential. God saved, we didn't save ourselves.

2. **Called us to a holy calling:** God initiates the call. The calling is effective (Romans 8:28-30: all who are called are justified).

3. **Not because of our works:** Explicit denial that salvation is conditioned on human action.

4. **According to his own purpose and grace:** Salvation flows from God's purpose (decree) and grace (unmerited favor), not human merit or foreseen faith.

5. **Which he gave us in Christ Jesus:** Grace was given to us. When? "Before the ages began."

6. **Before the ages began:** Pre-creation, pre-temporal, pre-historic. God gave us grace "before the ages began"—before we existed, before we could do anything good or bad, before we could believe or disbelieve. Election is unconditional and eternal.

7. **Manifested through appearing of Savior:** What was hidden in God's decree before creation is now revealed in history through Christ's incarnation. The gospel reveals what God decreed before time.

**God's Elect (2 Timothy 2:10):** "Therefore I endure everything for the sake of the elect, that they also may obtain the salvation that is in Christ Jesus with eternal glory."

Paul speaks of "the elect"—a definite group whom God chose. "That they also may obtain the salvation"—Paul endures so that the elect will obtain salvation. Their salvation is certain (God chose them), but God uses means (Paul's ministry) to bring it about.

**The Lord Knows Those Who Are His (2 Timothy 2:19):** "But God's firm foundation stands, bearing this seal: 'The Lord knows those who are his,' and, 'Let everyone who names the name of the Lord depart from iniquity.'"

"The Lord knows those who are his"—definite, particular knowledge. God doesn't just know about them; He knows them as His own. This is election knowledge (Amos 3:2: "You only have I known of all the families of the earth"). 

The foundation (God's saving purpose) stands firm regardless of false professors. The seal authenticates: (1) God knows His own, (2) Those who are His depart from iniquity. Both God's sovereign choice and human moral transformation are affirmed.

**God May Grant Repentance (2 Timothy 2:24-26):** "And the Lord's servant must not be quarrelsome but kind to everyone, able to teach, patiently enduring evil, correcting his opponents with gentleness. God may perhaps grant them repentance leading to a knowledge of the truth, and they may come to their senses and escape from the snare of the devil, after being captured by him to do his will."

**Critical theology:**

1. **God may perhaps grant repentance:** Repentance is granted by God, not self-generated. "May perhaps" acknowledges God's sovereignty—He grants repentance to whom He wills.

2. **Repentance leads to knowledge:** Sequence matters. God grants repentance, which leads to knowledge of truth. Not: knowledge produces repentance. Rather: God-given repentance produces knowledge.

3. **Captured by the devil:** Before conversion, people are "captured" by Satan "to do his will." This is bondage, not libertarian freedom. Total inability is assumed.

4. **Escape from the snare:** God's granting repentance results in escape. The power to escape is God's; the repentance is His gift.

**All Scripture Breathed Out by God (2 Timothy 3:16-17):** "All Scripture is breathed out by God and profitable for teaching, for reproof, for correction, and for training in righteousness, that the man of God may be complete, equipped for every good work."

"All Scripture is breathed out by God" (Greek: *theopneustos*—God-breathed). Scripture originates with God, not human invention. God's sovereign inspiration guarantees Scripture's authority and sufficiency.

"That the man of God may be complete, equipped for every good work"—God's Word equips believers for obedience. The Word is the means; God's Spirit is the power.

**The Lord Will Rescue (2 Timothy 4:18):** "The Lord will rescue me from every evil deed and bring me safely to his heavenly kingdom. To him be the glory forever and ever. Amen."

"The Lord will rescue"—confidence in God's sovereign preservation. Paul doesn't say "I hope I'll persevere" but "the Lord will rescue." Salvation and perseverance are God's work, certain and secure.

---

### Titus: Not Because of Our Works, But According to His Mercy

Titus is Paul's concentrated exposition of salvation by grace alone, particularly focusing on God's sovereign mercy in saving rebels and transforming them for good works.

**God's Elect, Promised Before Ages Began (Titus 1:1-3):** "Paul, a servant of God and an apostle of Jesus Christ, for the sake of the faith of God's elect and their knowledge of the truth, which accords with godliness, in hope of eternal life, which God, who never lies, promised before the ages began and at the proper time manifested in his word through the preaching with which I have been entrusted by the command of God our Savior."

**Packed with sovereignty:**

1. **God's elect:** Paul's apostleship is "for the sake of the faith of God's elect." There is a definite group—"God's elect"—chosen by God before they believed. Paul's mission is to bring them to faith.

2. **Their knowledge of the truth:** "Their knowledge"—the elect's knowledge. Knowledge of truth belongs to the elect; it's their possession as a result of election.

3. **In hope of eternal life:** The hope is certain because it rests on God's promise, not human performance.

4. **Which God... promised before the ages began:** God promised eternal life "before the ages began" (Greek: *pro chronōn aiōniōn*—before eternal times). Before creation, before humanity existed, before anyone could do anything good or bad, God promised eternal life. To whom? To His elect.

5. **God, who never lies:** The promise is absolutely certain because God cannot lie (Numbers 23:19; Hebrews 6:18). What God decreed before time, He will accomplish in time.

6. **At the proper time manifested:** God's eternal decree is revealed "at the proper time"—God's sovereign timing. The gospel reveals in history what God decreed in eternity.

7. **Through the preaching with which I have been entrusted:** God uses means (preaching) to accomplish His decreed purposes. Paul is entrusted with preaching, but the power to save is God's.

This one sentence demolishes synergism: Salvation was promised before time began, promised to God's elect, and is certain because God cannot lie. Human cooperation plays no role in the eternal decree.

**Sound Doctrine and Pure Conscience (Titus 1:9, 15-16):** "He must hold firm to the trustworthy word as taught, so that he may be able to give instruction in sound doctrine and also to rebuke those who contradict it... To the pure, all things are pure, but to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; but both their minds and their consciences are defiled. They profess to know God, but they deny him by their works. They are detestable, disobedient, unfit for any good work."

"To the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; but both their minds and their consciences are defiled"—total depravity. The unregenerate have defiled minds and consciences. They can't perceive spiritual truth rightly or judge morally with pure conscience. This is total inability applied to mind and conscience.

"They profess to know God, but they deny him by their works"—false profession. Works prove the profession false. This is the same principle as James 2—genuine faith produces genuine works; false profession produces nothing.

**Older Women Teaching What Is Good (Titus 2:3-5):** "Older women likewise are to be reverent in behavior, not slanderers or slaves to much wine. They are to teach what is good, and so train the young women to love their husbands and children, to be self-controlled, pure, working at home, kind, and submitting to their own husbands, that the word of God may not be reviled."

Godly living serves God's purpose: "that the word of God may not be reviled." Holy living adorns the gospel and protects God's reputation. But this holy living is the fruit of grace (2:11-12), not the cause of it.

**The Grace of God Has Appeared (Titus 2:11-14):** "For the grace of God has appeared, bringing salvation for all people, training us to renounce ungodliness and worldly passions, and to live self-controlled, upright, and godly lives in the present age, waiting for our blessed hope, the appearing of the glory of our great God and Savior Jesus Christ, who gave himself for us to redeem us from all lawlessness and to purify for himself a people for his own possession who are zealous for good works."

**This is one of Scripture's most comprehensive salvation statements:**

1. **The grace of God has appeared:** Grace is personified in Christ's incarnation. "Has appeared" (Greek: *epiphanē*—epiphany, manifestation). God's grace wasn't just taught or offered—it **appeared** in Christ.

2. **Bringing salvation for all people:** Does "all people" mean every individual without exception? Context and grammar say no. "All people" (Greek: *pasin anthrōpois*) is qualitative, not quantitative—all kinds of people (Jew and Gentile, slave and free, male and female), not every individual. If it meant every individual and grace actually brings salvation (not just makes it possible), universalism would follow.

   Compare Titus 1:1: Paul's ministry is "for the sake of the faith of God's elect." The elect are the "all people" whom grace saves—all kinds among the elect.

3. **Training us:** Grace doesn't just offer salvation and leave us unchanged. Grace **trains** (Greek: *paideuō*—disciplines, educates, instructs). God's grace actively works in believers to produce holiness.

4. **To renounce ungodliness:** Grace teaches us to say "no" to sin. But this isn't autonomous human will saying no—it's grace-empowered refusal. Grace produces the renunciation.

5. **And to live self-controlled, upright, and godly lives:** Grace produces three-fold godliness: self-controlled (internally), upright (relationally), godly (toward God). All three are grace's work, not human achievement.

6. **In the present age:** Between Christ's first and second comings, grace trains believers for holy living.

7. **Waiting for our blessed hope:** "Blessed hope" is Christ's return (2:13: "the appearing of the glory of our great God and Savior Jesus Christ"). The hope is certain because Christ will surely return.

8. **Who gave himself for us:** Christ's self-giving was voluntary and purposeful. "For us"—definite atonement. Christ gave Himself for His people specifically, not humanity abstractly.

9. **To redeem us from all lawlessness:** Purpose clause #1. Christ's death had a definite purpose—**redeem** (purchase, ransom). Redemption accomplishes freedom from lawlessness; it doesn't merely make freedom possible.

10. **And to purify for himself a people:** Purpose clause #2. Christ's death purifies a people—not potentially, but actually. He purifies "for himself"—they become His possession.

11. **A people for his own possession:** This is election language. God's elect are His "own possession" (Greek: *periousion*—special, treasured possession). Echoes Exodus 19:5; Deuteronomy 7:6; 14:2; 26:18; Malachi 3:17; 1 Peter 2:9. God's people are His treasured possession, chosen before the foundation of the world.

12. **Who are zealous for good works:** Good works are the result of redemption and purification, not their cause. Christ redeems and purifies **so that** His people are zealous for good works. The zeal is produced by grace, not self-generated.

**Theological summary of Titus 2:11-14:**
- Grace appeared in Christ (incarnation)
- Grace brings salvation (accomplishment, not mere possibility)
- Grace trains for godliness (sanctification)
- Christ gave Himself to redeem (definite atonement)
- Christ purifies a people for Himself (particular redemption)
- The redeemed are zealous for good works (fruit, not cause)

Every element is monergistic. Human cooperation appears nowhere. Grace does it all.

**Avoid Foolish Controversies (Titus 3:9-11):** "But avoid foolish controversies, genealogies, dissensions, and quarrels about the law, for they are unprofitable and worthless. As for a person who stirs up division, after warning him once and then twice, have nothing more to do with him, knowing that such a person is warped and sinful; he is self-condemned."

"He is self-condemned"—the divisive person condemns himself by his actions. This doesn't mean God plays no role in judgment, but that the person's sin brings condemnation. God's judgment is just because the person's actions warrant it.

**We Were Foolish, But God Saved Us (Titus 3:3-7):** "For we ourselves were once foolish, disobedient, led astray, slaves to various passions and pleasures, passing our days in malice and envy, hated by others and hating one another. But when the goodness and loving kindness of God our Savior appeared, he saved us, not because of works done by us in righteousness, but according to his own mercy, by the washing of regeneration and renewal of the Holy Spirit, whom he poured out on us richly through Jesus Christ our Savior, so that being justified by his grace we might become heirs according to the hope of eternal life."

**This is Paul's most concentrated statement of salvation theology. Every clause matters:**

**BEFORE SALVATION—Total Depravity (3:3):**

1. **Foolish:** Without spiritual understanding (1 Corinthians 2:14: "The natural person does not accept the things of the Spirit of God... he is not able to understand them").

2. **Disobedient:** In active rebellion against God's law.

3. **Led astray:** Deceived, wandering from truth. Not neutral seekers but deceived rebels.

4. **Slaves to various passions and pleasures:** Not free to choose God—enslaved to sin. Jesus: "Everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" (John 8:34). Paul: "You were slaves of sin" (Romans 6:17).

5. **Passing our days in malice and envy:** Constant state of sinfulness, not occasional lapses.

6. **Hated by others and hating one another:** Broken relationships, hostility. Total depravity affects all human relationships.

This is comprehensive description of unregenerate humanity. No seeking God (Romans 3:11), no ability to come to Christ (John 6:44), enslaved to sin (Romans 6:17-20), under God's wrath (Ephesians 2:3).

**THE TURNING POINT—God's Sovereign Intervention (3:4):**

**"But when the goodness and loving kindness of God our Savior appeared"**—massive contrast. "But" signals the change. Not "when we sought God" or "when we chose to cooperate"—"when... God appeared."

- **Goodness** (Greek: *chrēstotēs*): God's benevolence, kindness, generosity toward undeserving rebels
- **Loving kindness** (Greek: *philanthrōpia*): God's love for humanity, His merciful disposition
- **God our Savior:** Salvation belongs to God; He is the Savior
- **Appeared:** Historical manifestation in Christ's incarnation

God's initiative alone changes the situation. While we were foolish, disobedient slaves, God appeared. Not after we improved, not when we cooperated—while we were still sinners (Romans 5:8).

**SALVATION ACCOMPLISHED—Monergistic Grace (3:5-7):**

**Verse 5a: "He saved us"**
- Past tense—completed action, accomplished salvation
- "He saved"—active verb, God as subject
- "Us"—Paul and all believers; we are recipients, not contributors
- Not "He enabled us to save ourselves" or "He made salvation possible"—"He **saved** us"

**Verse 5b: "Not because of works done by us in righteousness"**
- Explicit exclusion of human merit
- "Not because of works"—no human contribution, not even partially
- "Done by us in righteousness"—even if we had done righteous works (which we didn't in our enslaved state), they wouldn't cause salvation
- This demolishes synergism: if salvation were even 1% human cooperation, it would be "because of works" to that degree. Paul says: zero percent works.

**Verse 5c: "But according to his own mercy"**
- "But"—contrasts with "not because of works"
- "According to his own mercy"—salvation flows from God's mercy, not human merit
- "His own"—emphasizes that mercy is God's possession and prerogative. He distributes it according to His will (Exodus 33:19: "I will have mercy on whom I have mercy")
- "Mercy"—compassion toward those in misery. We were in the misery of sin; God had mercy

**Verse 5d: "By the washing of regeneration"**
- "By"—instrumental. This is the means God uses to save
- "Washing" (Greek: *loutron*)—cleansing, purification. God washes away sin
- "Regeneration" (Greek: *palingenesia*—*palin* = again, *genesis* = birth). Literally: "new birth" or "being born again"
- This is the same concept as John 3:3-7 (must be born again), James 1:18 (of His own will He brought us forth), 1 Peter 1:3 (caused us to be born again)
- **Regeneration is monergistic:** Babies don't contribute to their physical birth; believers don't contribute to their spiritual birth. God births; we are born.

**Verse 5e: "And renewal of the Holy Spirit"**
- "Renewal" (Greek: *anakainōsis*): making new, renovation, transformation
- "Of the Holy Spirit"—the Spirit is the agent who renews. The Spirit doesn't merely assist our renewal; He accomplishes it
- The Spirit's work is renewal—making new what was old, dead, corrupted. This is new creation (2 Corinthians 5:17)

**Verse 6: "Whom he poured out on us richly through Jesus Christ our Savior"**
- "Whom"—refers to the Holy Spirit (verse 5)
- "He poured out"—God pours; we receive. Passive recipients of the Spirit's outpouring
- "On us"—not "offered to us" or "made available to us"—"poured out **on** us." The Spirit is given, not just offered
- "Richly"—abundantly, lavishly, generously. Not trickle but flood. Not minimal enablement but abundant empowering
- "Through Jesus Christ our Savior"—Christ is the mediator through whom the Spirit is given. The Spirit comes because of Christ's finished work

**Verse 7a: "So that being justified by his grace"**
- "So that"—purpose clause. God saves, regenerates, renews, pours out the Spirit **so that** we are justified
- "Being justified"—present passive participle. We are being declared righteous (forensic justification). God declares; we are declared.
- "By his grace"—grace is both the source and the means. Not grace + works, not grace + cooperation—grace alone
- **Justification:** God's legal declaration that sinners are righteous based on Christ's righteousness credited to their account (Romans 4:3-5; 2 Corinthians 5:21; Philippians 3:9)

**Verse 7b: "We might become heirs according to the hope of eternal life"**
- "We might become heirs"—result of justification. Justified people are heirs
- "According to the hope"—the hope is certain because it rests on God's promise (1:2: "promised before the ages began")
- "Of eternal life"—the inheritance is eternal life, guaranteed to heirs

**Theological Summary of Titus 3:3-7:**

**The Gospel in Seven Movements:**
1. **We were:** Totally depraved—foolish, disobedient, enslaved, hating (v. 3)
2. **But God:** Took initiative—His goodness and love appeared (v. 4)
3. **He saved:** Accomplished salvation—past tense, completed (v. 5a)
4. **Not by works:** Excluded all human merit—zero contribution (v. 5b)
5. **But by mercy:** According to His sovereign grace alone (v. 5c)
6. **Through regeneration:** By new birth and Spirit's renewal (vv. 5d-6)
7. **Result:** Justified, heirs of eternal life (v. 7)

**Every element is God's work:**
- God appeared
- He saved
- His mercy
- He washes (regeneration)
- Spirit renews
- He pours out Spirit
- His grace justifies
- We become heirs

**No human cooperation anywhere:**
- Not our seeking (we were led astray)
- Not our works (explicitly excluded)
- Not our faith generating salvation (faith is the instrument to receive what God gives, but God gives regeneration, Spirit, justification)
- Not our decision activating grace (grace actively saves while we're still foolish slaves)

**This passage alone destroys synergism.** If you can find human cooperation in Titus 3:3-7, you can find it anywhere. You can't. It's not there.

**The Saying Is Trustworthy (Titus 3:8):** "The saying is trustworthy, and I want you to insist on these things, so that those who have believed in God may be careful to devote themselves to good works. These things are excellent and profitable for people."

"The saying is trustworthy"—what saying? The gospel just stated in 3:3-7. This is completely reliable, absolutely certain, worthy of full confidence.

"So that those who have believed in God may be careful to devote themselves to good works"—the purpose of insisting on the gospel (salvation by mercy alone, not works) is to produce good works. Paradox: preaching salvation by grace alone produces the most zealous good works. Why? Because grace transforms; law only condemns. Those saved by grace are liberated to serve out of gratitude, not fear or merit-seeking.

"These things are excellent and profitable"—the gospel truths Paul has expounded are beneficial. Sound doctrine produces godly living.

**Greet Those Who Love Us in the Faith (Titus 3:15):** "All who are with me send greetings to you. Greet those who love us in the faith. Grace be with you all."

"Grace be with you all"—Paul's letters typically end with grace. Why? Because everything—from election before time (1:2) to final perseverance to glory—is grace. Grace opens, grace sustains, grace completes.

### Summary: Titus' Concentrated Soteriology

Titus presents salvation as:
- **Eternally decreed:** Promised before ages began (1:2)
- **Historically accomplished:** God's grace appeared in Christ (2:11; 3:4)
- **Monergistically applied:** He saved us, not we ourselves (3:5)
- **Spirit-empowered:** Spirit poured out richly (3:6)
- **Grace-centered:** Not by works, but by mercy and grace (3:5, 7)
- **Transformational:** Producing good works and godliness (2:12, 14; 3:8)
- **Eschatologically certain:** Heirs according to hope of eternal life (3:7)

**Synergism has no foothold in Titus.** Every salvation statement attributes everything to God's sovereign, merciful, gracious, monergistic work. From eternal election to final glorification, it's all grace.

The entire book is Paul saying: "God did it all. We contributed nothing but the sin that needed saving. To Him be all glory."

---

### Philemon: Providence in Personal Relationships

Though Philemon doesn't contain explicit theological discourse on sovereignty, the entire situation demonstrates God's providential ordering of events for redemptive purposes.

**Providence Transforms Evil Into Good (Philemon 15-16):** "For this perhaps is why he was parted from you for a while, that you might have him back forever, no longer as a bondservant but more than a bondservant, as a beloved brother—especially to me, but how much more to you, both in the flesh and in the Lord."

Paul interprets Onesimus's flight (a sinful act) as within God's providence: "perhaps this is why he was parted from you." The language is cautious, but the theology is clear—God orchestrated circumstances (Onesimus fleeing, meeting Paul, being converted) to accomplish a greater good (reconciliation and transformation from slave to brother). This is the same pattern as Joseph: "You meant evil... but God meant it for good" (Genesis 50:20).

**Divine Passive—God's Hidden Hand (Philemon 15):** "He was parted from you" (passive voice)—not "he ran away" (though he did). Paul uses divine passive construction, common in Scripture, to indicate God's sovereign hand behind events without explicitly naming God as the agent. Compare: "The lot is cast into the lap, but its every decision is from the LORD" (Proverbs 16:33).

**God Works Through Human Persuasion (Philemon 8-14):** Paul could command Philemon by apostolic authority (v. 8), but instead appeals (v. 9) so that Philemon's "goodness might not be by compulsion but of your own accord" (v. 14). This models how God works—He ordains both ends and means. God decreed Philemon would receive Onesimus, and He uses Paul's appeal as the means. Divine sovereignty and human responsibility/willing cooperation coexist.

**Confidence in God's Purpose (Philemon 21):** "Confident of your obedience, I write to you, knowing that you will do even more than I say." Paul's confidence isn't in Philemon's natural goodness, but in God's work in Philemon (cf. Philippians 2:13: "it is God who works in you, both to will and to work"). This epistle demonstrates that God's sovereignty extends even to personal relationships, not just cosmic events.

---

## IX. General Epistles: Confirming Testimony

### Hebrews: Jesus, Founder and Perfecter

**Christ Upholds the Universe (Hebrews 1:3)**: "He is the radiance of the glory of God and the exact imprint of his nature, and he upholds the universe by the word of his power. After making purification for sins, he sat down at the right hand of the Majesty on high."

Christ "upholds the universe by the word of his power"—active, moment-by-moment sustaining of all creation. Not deistic absenteeism; Christ actively holds all things in existence by His sovereign power (Colossians 1:17: "in him all things hold together"). If Christ sovereignly upholds the universe, He sovereignly accomplishes salvation.

**Jesus Made Perfect Through Suffering (Hebrews 2:10)**: "For it was fitting that he, for whom and by whom all things exist, in bringing many sons to glory, should make the founder of their salvation perfect through suffering."

"For whom and by whom all things exist"—God is the source and goal of all creation. "Bringing many sons to glory"—God brings them; they don't bring themselves. Definite atonement for "many sons" (not all without exception, but the elect). Jesus is "the founder of their salvation"—He authors, originates, accomplishes it.

**Making Propitiation for the People (Hebrews 2:17)**: "Therefore he had to be made like his brothers in every respect, so that he might become a merciful and faithful high priest in the service of God, to make propitiation for the sins of the people."

"To make propitiation for the sins of the people"—Christ's priestly work satisfies God's wrath for "the people" (definite group). Not for all humanity without exception, but for God's covenant people. The propitiation is accomplished, not merely offered.

**God's Unchangeable Purpose (Hebrews 6:17-20)**: "So when God desired to show more convincingly to the heirs of the promise the unchangeable character of his purpose, he guaranteed it with an oath, so that by two unchangeable things, in which it is impossible for God to lie, we who have fled for refuge might have strong encouragement to hold fast to the hope set before us. We have this as a sure and steadfast anchor of the soul, a hope that enters into the inner place behind the curtain, where Jesus has gone as a forerunner on our behalf, having become a high priest forever after the order of Melchizedek."

"The unchangeable character of his purpose"—God's decree cannot be altered. "Two unchangeable things" (promise and oath) guarantee the outcome because "it is impossible for God to lie." Our hope is "sure and steadfast" because it rests on God's unchangeable purpose, not our changeable performance. Jesus entered as "forerunner on our behalf"—He guarantees our entrance because He entered first.

**Christ Saves to the Uttermost (Hebrews 7:23-25)**: "The former priests were many in number, because they were prevented by death from continuing in office, but he holds his priesthood permanently, because he continues forever. Consequently, he is able to save to the uttermost those who draw near to God through him, since he always lives to make intercession for them."

"He is able to save to the uttermost"—complete, final, eternal salvation. Not partial, not potential, but complete. For whom? "Those who draw near to God through him"—but who draws near? Those whom the Father draws (John 6:44) and grants (John 6:65).

"Since he always lives to make intercession for them"—Christ's perpetual intercession guarantees perseverance. He prays for His elect (John 17:9: "I am praying for them. I am not praying for the world but for those whom you have given me"), and His prayers are always answered (John 11:42). Therefore, those for whom He intercedes will certainly be saved to the uttermost.

**New Covenant Written on Hearts (Hebrews 8:10-12)**: "For this is the covenant that I will make with the house of Israel after those days, declares the Lord: I will put my laws into their minds, and write them on their hearts, and I will be their God, and they shall be my people. And they shall not teach, each one his neighbor and each one his brother, saying, 'Know the Lord,' for they shall all know me, from the least of them to the greatest. For I will be merciful toward their iniquities, and I will remember their sins no more."

Quoting Jeremiah 31:31-34. The New Covenant is entirely monergistic: "I will put... I will write... I will be their God... they shall be my people... they shall all know me... I will be merciful... I will remember their sins no more." Eight divine actions, zero human contributions. God accomplishes everything the covenant promises.

**Obtained Eternal Redemption (Hebrews 9:12, 15)**: "He entered once for all into the holy places, not by means of the blood of goats and calves but by means of his own blood, thus securing an eternal redemption... Therefore he is the mediator of a new covenant, so that those who are called may receive the promised eternal inheritance, since a death has occurred that redeems them from the transgressions committed under the first covenant."

"Securing an eternal redemption"—not "making redemption possible," but "securing" it (obtaining, accomplishing). Past tense—accomplished. "Eternal redemption"—cannot be lost. Christ's death actually redeems "those who are called" from their transgressions. Definite atonement: His death redeems those the Father called.

**We Have Been Sanctified (Hebrews 10:10, 14)**: "And by that will we have been sanctified through the offering of the body of Jesus Christ once for all... For by a single offering he has perfected for all time those who are being sanctified."

"We have been sanctified"—perfect tense, completed action with continuing results. Sanctification (in the positional sense—set apart as holy) is accomplished through Christ's offering. "He has perfected for all time those who are being sanctified"—definite accomplishment. Christ's single offering perfected (made complete, brought to the goal) those being sanctified. Not "might perfect if they persevere," but "has perfected." The atonement succeeds for all whom Christ intended to save.

**Jesus, Founder and Perfecter of Faith (Hebrews 12:2)**: "Looking to Jesus, the founder and perfecter of our faith, who for the joy that was set before him endured the cross, despising the shame, and is seated at the right hand of the throne of God."

Jesus is the "founder" (archēgos—author, originator, source) and "perfecter" (teleiōtēs—completer, finisher) of our faith. Faith doesn't originate in us—Jesus is its source. And He completes it—brings it to its goal. From start to finish, faith is His work. We exercise faith, but He authors and perfects it. This demolishes the idea that faith is our independent contribution to salvation.

**God Equips and Works in Us (Hebrews 13:20-21)**: "Now may the God of peace who brought again from the dead our Lord Jesus, the great shepherd of the sheep, by the blood of the eternal covenant, equip you with everything good that you may do his will, working in us that which is pleasing in his sight, through Jesus Christ, to whom be glory forever and ever. Amen."

God equips us; God works in us. The good works that please God are "that which is pleasing in his sight"—and God Himself works these in us. Not self-generated human effort producing good works, but God working in us to produce what pleases Him (Philippians 2:13: "For it is God who works in you, both to will and to work for his good pleasure"). Even our willing and working are God's work in us.

---

### James: Of His Own Will He Brought Us Forth

**Of His Own Will He Brought Us Forth (James 1:17-18)**: "Every good gift and every perfect gift is from above, coming down from the Father of lights, with whom there is no variation or shadow due to change. Of his own will he brought us forth by the word of truth, that we should be a kind of firstfruits of his creatures."

Packed with sovereignty:

1. **Every good gift from above**: Including faith, repentance, salvation. If faith were self-generated, it wouldn't be a gift from above.

2. **Father of lights with no variation**: Immutability. God's purposes don't shift based on human decisions.

3. **Of HIS OWN will**: "Of his own will he brought us forth"—not of our will (John 1:13: "not of the will of man, but of God"). Regeneration originates in God's sovereign will, not human decision.

4. **He brought us forth**: Active verb, God as subject. We don't bring ourselves forth. "Brought forth" is birth language—regeneration, new birth. God regenerates by His power.

5. **By the word of truth**: The means is the Word, but the power is God's. The Word is the instrument; God is the agent who brings forth.

6. **That we should be firstfruits**: Purpose clause. God's regenerating work has a purpose—that we would be His firstfruits, dedicated to Him. We are the harvest of His sovereign grace.

**The Implanted Word (James 1:21)**: "Therefore put away all filth and rampant wickedness and receive with meekness the implanted word, which is able to save your souls."

"The implanted word, which is able to save your souls"—the Word must be implanted (by God) to save. Humans can't implant the Word in themselves. This is God's work through the means of the Word. "Receive with meekness"—the proper posture is receptivity, not autonomous generation of faith.

**God Chose the Poor (James 2:5)**: "Listen, my beloved brothers, has not God chosen those who are poor in the world to be rich in faith and heirs of the kingdom, which he has promised to those who love him?"

"Has not God **chosen**"—election language. God chose the poor "to be rich in faith"—faith is the result of God's choosing, not its cause. God's election produces faith and inheritance. "Heirs of the kingdom, which he has promised to those who love him"—inheritance comes by promise (God's decree), and even the love for God is fruit of being chosen (1 John 4:19: "We love because he first loved us").

**Faith Without Works Is Dead (James 2:14-26)**: James addresses false profession, not synergism. "What good is it, my brothers, if someone **says** he has faith but does not have works? Can **that** faith save him?" (2:14). "If someone **says**"—mere profession. "Can **that** faith"—the demonstrative points to dead, professed faith. Answer: no.

"Faith by itself, if it does not have works, is dead" (2:17). Not "doesn't exist" but "is dead"—a corpse. It looks like faith but has no life. Genuine faith (living) always produces works. Dead faith (mere profession) produces nothing.

**Two senses of "justified"**: Paul uses "justified" forensically (declared righteous before God—Romans 4:3-5). James uses "justified" evidentially (shown to be righteous before men—James 2:18: "Show me your faith"). Both are right; different questions. Paul asks: "How is a sinner declared righteous before God?" Answer: By faith alone, apart from works (Romans 3:28; 4:5). James asks: "How does someone prove their faith is genuine?" Answer: By works that flow from faith.

Timeline: Genesis 15:6 (Abraham believed, counted righteous) occurred **before** Genesis 22 (Abraham offered Isaac). Paul cites Genesis 15:6 to show justification by faith. James cites the same verse but says it was "fulfilled" in Genesis 22—the faith declared in Genesis 15:6 proved itself genuine in Genesis 22. Works flow from faith and demonstrate it; they don't contribute to justification.

James fights false profession (2:19: "Even the demons believe—and shudder!"), not Pauline soteriology. True faith transforms; false profession leaves unchanged. James and Paul agree: cause of justification is faith alone; evidence of genuine faith is works; power producing works is God's grace (Ephesians 2:10: "created in Christ Jesus for good works, which God prepared beforehand").

**God Gives Grace to the Humble (James 4:6)**: "But he gives more grace. Therefore it says, 'God opposes the proud but gives grace to the humble.'"

"He gives more grace"—God is the giver. God's sovereign distribution of grace. But who are the humble? Those whom God has humbled (Matthew 18:4). Even humility is God's work (Philippians 2:13).

**If the Lord Wills (James 4:13-15)**: "Come now, you who say, 'Today or tomorrow we will go into such and such a town and spend a year there and trade and make a profit'—yet you do not know what tomorrow will bring. What is your life? For you are a mist that appears for a little time and then vanishes. Instead you ought to say, 'If the Lord wills, we will live and do this or that.'"

All life, all plans depend on God's sovereign will. Nothing happens unless God wills it. Not just spiritual matters—"we will live" depends on God's will. Every breath, every moment exists because God decrees it.
---

### 1 Peter: Elect According to Foreknowledge

**Elect According to Foreknowledge (1 Peter 1:1-2)**: "To those who are elect exiles of the Dispersion in Pontus, Galatia, Cappadocia, Asia, and Bithynia, according to the foreknowledge of God the Father, in the sanctification of the Spirit, for obedience to Jesus Christ and for sprinkling with his blood."

"Elect... according to the foreknowledge of God." "Foreknowledge" (prognosis) in Scripture means more than mere awareness—it means foreordaining, pre-determining love (cf. Romans 8:29; 11:2). Election precedes and causes sanctification and obedience.

**Caused to Be Born Again (1 Peter 1:3)**: "Blessed be the God and Father of our Lord Jesus Christ! According to his great mercy, he has caused us to be born again to a living hope through the resurrection of Jesus Christ from the dead."

"He has CAUSED us to be born again." Birth is not self-generated—it is caused by God. Monergistic regeneration.

**Destined to Stumble (1 Peter 2:8)**: "And 'A stone of stumbling, and a rock of offense.' They stumble because they disobey the word, as they were destined to do."

"They were destined to do"—their stumbling is within God's decree. Not just foreseen but foreordained. This doesn't remove their responsibility (they stumble "because they disobey"), but it places their disobedience within God's sovereign plan.

**God Guards (1 Peter 5:10)**: "And after you have suffered a little while, the God of all grace, who has called you to his eternal glory in Christ, will himself restore, confirm, strengthen, and establish you."

God "will himself" do all these things. Perseverance is guaranteed because God Himself guards and establishes His people.

---

### 2 Peter: Divine Power Grants All Things for Life and Godliness

**Faith Obtained by Divine Allotment (2 Peter 1:1)**: "Simeon Peter, a servant and apostle of Jesus Christ, To those who have obtained a faith of equal standing with ours by the righteousness of our God and Savior Jesus Christ."

"To those who have obtained a faith"—faith is obtained, not self-generated. The verb (Greek: *lagchanō*) means "to receive by lot, to obtain by divine allotment." Faith is God's gift, distributed according to His sovereign will. "By the righteousness of our God and Savior"—faith comes through Christ's righteousness, not our own. We obtain faith because God is righteous (He keeps His promises to save His elect), not because we are righteous.

**Divine Power Has Granted All Things (2 Peter 1:3-4)**: "His divine power has granted to us all things that pertain to life and godliness, through the knowledge of him who called us to his own glory and excellence, by which he has granted to us his precious and very great promises, so that through them you may become partakers of the divine nature, having escaped from the corruption that is in the world because of sinful desire."

Absolutely packed with monergism:

1. **His divine power has granted**: Perfect tense—completed action with ongoing results. God's power has already granted everything needed. Not "will grant if you cooperate" but "has granted."

2. **All things that pertain to life and godliness**: Everything needed for salvation (life) and sanctification (godliness) has been granted by God. No human contribution needed—God has granted **all things**.

3. **Through the knowledge of him**: Saving knowledge is the means, but God grants it. We don't generate knowledge of God; He reveals Himself.

4. **Who called us**: Divine calling. God called us "to his own glory and excellence"—for His purposes, His glory.

5. **He has granted precious promises**: The promises are God's gift. We don't earn them or activate them—He grants them.

6. **So that through them you may become partakers**: Purpose clause. God grants promises **so that** we become partakers of divine nature. The promises accomplish God's purpose; they don't merely enable our cooperation.

7. **Having escaped from corruption**: Escape from corruption is the result of God's granted promises, not human effort to escape.

**Confirm Your Calling and Election (2 Peter 1:10-11)**: "Therefore, brothers, be all the more diligent to confirm your calling and election, for if you practice these qualities you will never fall. For in this way there will be richly provided for you an entrance into the eternal kingdom of our Lord and Savior Jesus Christ."

"Confirm your calling and election"—not "secure" your election (that's impossible—God's decree stands), but "confirm" it (make it evident, prove it genuine). Growth in godliness (1:5-9) demonstrates that God's calling and election are real in your life.

"If you practice these qualities you will never fall"—God's work produces qualities; the qualities prove God's work. The promise is certain: practicing God-given qualities = never falling. This is perseverance guaranteed by God's power working through means (the qualities He produces).

"There will be richly provided for you"—passive voice. God provides entrance into the kingdom. We don't earn it; He richly provides it.

**No Prophecy by Human Will (2 Peter 1:20-21)**: "Knowing this first of all, that no prophecy of Scripture comes from someone's own interpretation. For no prophecy was ever produced by the will of man, but men spoke from God as they were carried along by the Holy Spirit."

"No prophecy was ever produced by the will of man"—explicit denial of human origination. "But men spoke from God"—God is the source. "As they were carried along by the Holy Spirit"—the Spirit carried (bore along, moved) the prophets. They spoke, but the Spirit directed what they spoke.
